<td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.berlin.de/en/">berlin.de</a></td>

</table>
<p><b>Berlin</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span></span>-/</a></span></span>, <small>German:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[bɛɐ̯ˈliːn]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Berlin.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/De-Berlin.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Berlin.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and the largest city of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> as well as one of its 16 constituent <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">states</a>. With a population of approximately 3.7 million,<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">[4]</a></sup> Berlin is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_in_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest cities in the European Union by population within city limits">second most populous city proper</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the seventh <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_European_Union" title="List of urban areas in the European Union">most populous urban area</a> in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Insee_-_-_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insee_-_--5">[5]</a></sup> Located in northeastern Germany on the banks of the rivers <a href="/wiki/Spree" title="Spree">Spree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Havel" title="Havel">Havel</a>, it is the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin/Brandenburg_Metropolitan_Region" title="Berlin/Brandenburg Metropolitan Region">Berlin-Brandenburg Metropolitan Region</a>, which has roughly 6 million residents from more than 180 nations<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LUZ_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LUZ-9">[9]</a></sup>. Due to its location in the <a href="/wiki/European_Plain" title="European Plain">European Plain</a>, Berlin is influenced by a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> seasonal climate. Around one-third of the city's area is composed of forests, parks, gardens, rivers, canals and lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>First documented in the 13th century and situated at the crossing of two important historic <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-staple_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staple-11">[11]</a></sup> Berlin became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a> (1417–1701), the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> (1701–1918), the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> (1871–1918), the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> (1919–1933) and the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a> (1933–1945).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1920s_Berlin" title="1920s Berlin">Berlin in the 1920s</a> was the third largest municipality in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and its subsequent occupation by the victorious countries, the city was divided; <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a> was declared capital of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, while <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> became a de facto <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West German</a> <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a>, surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> (1961–1989) and East German territory.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> in 1990, Berlin once again became the capital of all of Germany.</p>
<p>Berlin is an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">international city</a> of culture, politics, media and science.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Its economy is based on <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high-tech</a> firms and the service sector, encompassing a diverse range of <a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">creative industries</a>, research facilities, media corporations and convention venues.<sup id="cite_ref-congress_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congress-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cityofdesign_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cityofdesign-20">[20]</a></sup> Berlin serves as a continental hub for air and rail traffic and has a highly complex public transportation network. The metropolis is a popular <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Germany" title="Tourism in Germany">tourist destination</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Significant industries also include <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">IT</a>, pharmaceuticals, biomedical engineering, clean tech, <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, construction and electronics.</p>
<p>Modern Berlin is home to world renowned universities, orchestras, museums, entertainment venues and is host to many sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-22">[22]</a></sup> Its urban setting has made it a sought-after location for international <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_Berlin" title="List of films set in Berlin">film productions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The city is well known for its festivals, diverse architecture, nightlife, contemporary arts and a <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_liveable_cities" title="World's most liveable cities">high quality of living</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Since the 2000s Berlin has seen the emergence of a cosmopolitan <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurial</a> <a href="/wiki/Startup_ecosystem" title="Startup ecosystem">scene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Berlin" title="History of Berlin">History of Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Berlin" title="Timeline of Berlin">Timeline of Berlin</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The name Berlin has its roots in the language of <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavic</a> inhabitants of the area of today's Berlin, and may be related to the Old <a href="/wiki/Polabian_language" title="Polabian language">Polabian</a> stem <i>berl-</i>/<i>birl-</i> ("swamp").<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> All German place names ending on <i>-ow</i>, <i>-itz</i> and <i>-in</i>, of which there are many east of the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">River Elbe</a>, are of <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> origin (<a href="/wiki/Germania_Slavica" title="Germania Slavica">Germania Slavica</a>). There are many boroughs of Slavic origin in the city: Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Karow_(Berlin)" title="Karow (Berlin)">Karow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Malchow_(Berlin)" title="Malchow (Berlin)">Malchow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Pankow" title="Pankow">Pankow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Spandau" title="Spandau">Spandau</a> (earlier: <i>Spandow</i>), Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Gatow" title="Gatow">Gatow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Kladow" title="Kladow">Kladow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Steglitz" title="Steglitz">Steglitz</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Lankwitz" title="Lankwitz">Lankwitz</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Britz" title="Britz">Britz</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Buckow_(Berlin)" title="Buckow (Berlin)">Buckow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Rudow" title="Rudow">Rudow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Alt-Treptow" title="Alt-Treptow">Alt-Treptow</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Schm%C3%B6ckwitz" title="Schmöckwitz">Schmöckwitz</a>, Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Marzahn" title="Marzahn">Marzahn</a> and Berlin-<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6penick" title="Köpenick">Köpenick</a>. Since the <i>Ber-</i> at the beginning sounds like the German word <i>Bär</i> (bear), a bear appears in the coat of arms of the city. It is therefore a <a href="/wiki/Canting_arms" title="Canting arms">canting arm</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="12th_to_16th_centuries">12th to 16th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 12th to 16th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg/220px-ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg/330px-ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg/440px-ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4961" data-file-height="3390" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ZLB-Berliner_Ansichten-Januar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Berlin in 1688</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earliest evidence of settlements in the area of today's Berlin are a wooden rod dated from approximately 1192<sup id="cite_ref-zycwaq_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zycwaq-27">[27]</a></sup> and leftovers of wooden houseparts dated to 1174 found in a 2012 excavation in Berlin Mitte.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The first written records of towns in the area of present-day Berlin date from the late 12th century. <a href="/wiki/Spandau" title="Spandau">Spandau</a> is first mentioned in 1197 and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6penick" title="Köpenick">Köpenick</a> in 1209, although these areas did not join Berlin until 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The central part of Berlin can be traced back to two towns. <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B6lln" title="Cölln">Cölln</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Fischerinsel" title="Fischerinsel">Fischerinsel</a> is first mentioned in a 1237 document, and Berlin, across the <a href="/wiki/Spree" title="Spree">Spree</a> in what is now called the <a href="/wiki/Nikolaiviertel" title="Nikolaiviertel">Nikolaiviertel</a>, is referenced in a document from 1244.<sup id="cite_ref-zycwaq_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zycwaq-27">[27]</a></sup> 1237 is considered the founding date of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Medtradc_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medtradc-30">[30]</a></sup> The two towns over time formed close economic and social ties, and profited from the <a href="/wiki/Staple_right" title="Staple right">staple right</a> on the two important <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Via_Imperii" title="Via Imperii">Via Imperii</a></i> and from <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> to <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-staple_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staple-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1307, they formed an alliance with a common external policy, their internal administrations still being separated.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C3.B6ver2010_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C3.B6ver2010-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lui_stadtgr_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lui_stadtgr-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1415 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick I</a> became the <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">elector</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a>, which he ruled until 1440.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> During the 15th century, his successors established Berlin-Cölln as capital of the margraviate, and subsequent members of the <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohenzollern">Hohenzollern</a> family ruled in Berlin until 1918, first as electors of Brandenburg, then as kings of Prussia, and eventually as <a href="/wiki/German_emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="German emperor">German emperors</a>. In 1443 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick II, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick II Irontooth</a> started the construction of a new <a href="/wiki/Stadtschloss,_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadtschloss, Berlin">royal palace</a> in the twin city Berlin-Cölln. The protests of the town citizens against the building culminated in 1448, in the "Berlin Indignation" ("Berliner Unwille").<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> This protest was not successful and the citizenry lost many of its political and economic privileges. After the royal palace was finished in 1451, it gradually came into use. From 1470, with the new elector <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_III_Achilles,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Albrecht III Achilles, Elector of Brandenburg">Albrecht III Achilles</a>, Berlin-Cölln became the new royal residence.<sup id="cite_ref-Lui_stadtgr_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lui_stadtgr-32">[32]</a></sup> Officially, the Berlin-Cölln palace became permanent residence of the Brandenburg electors of the Hohenzollerns from 1486, when <a href="/wiki/John_Cicero,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="John Cicero, Elector of Brandenburg">John Cicero</a> came to power.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Berlin-Cölln, however, had to give up its status as a free <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic</a> city. In 1539, the electors and the city officially became <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_to_19th_centuries">17th to 19th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 17th to 19th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg/170px-Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg/255px-Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg/340px-Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="596" data-file-height="730" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Friedrich_Zweite_Alt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> (1712–1786) was one of Europe's <a href="/wiki/Enlightened_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlightened monarch">enlightened monarchs</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> between 1618 and 1648 devastated Berlin. One third of its houses were damaged or destroyed, and the city lost half of its population.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick William I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick William</a>, known as the "Great Elector", who had succeeded his father <a href="/wiki/George_William,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="George William, Elector of Brandenburg">George William</a> as ruler in 1640, initiated a policy of promoting immigration and religious tolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-Carlyle1853_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carlyle1853-39">[39]</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Potsdam" title="Edict of Potsdam">Edict of Potsdam</a> in 1685, Frederick William offered asylum to the French <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Plaut1995_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plaut1995-40">[40]</a></sup> By 1700, approximately 30 percent of Berlin's residents were French, because of the Huguenot immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-Gray2007_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gray2007-41">[41]</a></sup> Many other immigrants came from <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Poland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Salzburg" title="Archbishopric of Salzburg">Salzburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cybriwsky2013_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cybriwsky2013-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg/220px-Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg/330px-Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg/440px-Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2549" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Unter_den_Linden_Victoria_Hotel_um_1900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Berlin became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in 1871 and expanded rapidly in the following years. (Unter den Linden in 1900)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1618 the Margraviate of Brandenburg had been in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duchy of Prussia</a>. In 1701 the dual state formed the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick III, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick III, Elector of Brandenburg</a> crowned himself as king <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Frederick I in Prussia</a>. Berlin became the capital of the new Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> replacing <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">Königsberg</a>. This was a successful attempt to centralise the capital in the very far-flung state, and it was the first time the city began to grow. In 1709, Berlin merged with the four cities of Cölln, Friedrichswerder, Friedrichstadt and Dorotheenstadt under the name Berlin, "Haupt- und Residenzstadt Berlin".<sup id="cite_ref-St.C3.B6ver2010_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C3.B6ver2010-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1740 Frederick II, known as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> (1740–1786), came to power.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1965_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1965-44">[44]</a></sup> Under the rule of Frederick II, Berlin became a center of <a href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" class="mw-redirect" title="The Enlightenment">the Enlightenment</a>, but also, was briefly occupied during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> by the Russian army.<sup id="cite_ref-PerryChase2012_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PerryChase2012-45">[45]</a></sup> Following France's victory in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition" title="War of the Fourth Coalition">War of the Fourth Coalition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> marched into Berlin in 1806, but granted self-government to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis2013_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis2013-46">[46]</a></sup> In 1815 the city became part of the new <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Brandenburg" title="Province of Brandenburg">Province of Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-StaffInc.2010_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StaffInc.2010-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> transformed Berlin during the 19th century; the city's economy and population expanded dramatically, and it became the main railway hub and economic centre of Germany. Additional suburbs soon developed and increased the area and population of Berlin. In 1861 neighbouring suburbs including <a href="/wiki/Wedding_(Berlin)" title="Wedding (Berlin)">Wedding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moabit" title="Moabit">Moabit</a> and several others were incorporated into Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-Schulte-Peevers2010_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schulte-Peevers2010-48">[48]</a></sup> In 1871 Berlin became capital of the newly founded <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-St.C3.B6ver2013_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St.C3.B6ver2013-49">[49]</a></sup> In 1881 it became a city district separate from Brandenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-Strassmann2008_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strassmann2008-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_to_21st_centuries">20th to 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 20th to 21st centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/1920s_Berlin" title="1920s Berlin">1920s Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirchner_1913_Street,_Berlin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg/150px-Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg/225px-Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg/300px-Kirchner_1913_Street%2C_Berlin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="337" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirchner_1913_Street,_Berlin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Street, Berlin</i> (1913) by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Ludwig_Kirchner" title="Ernst Ludwig Kirchner">Ernst Ludwig Kirchner</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 20th century, Berlin had become a fertile ground for the <a href="/wiki/German_Expressionism" title="German Expressionism">German Expressionist</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-HollandGawthrop2001_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HollandGawthrop2001-51">[51]</a></sup> In fields such as <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">cinema</a> new forms of artistic styles were invented. At the end of the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> in 1918, a <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">republic</a> was proclaimed by <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Scheidemann" title="Philipp Scheidemann">Philipp Scheidemann</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(building)" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichstag (building)">Reichstag building</a>. In 1920 the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Berlin_Act" title="Greater Berlin Act">Greater Berlin Act</a> incorporated dozens of suburban cities, villages and estates around Berlin into an expanded city. The act increased the area of Berlin from 66 to 883&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (25 to 341&#160;sq&#160;mi). The population almost doubled and Berlin had a population of around four million. During the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_culture" title="Weimar culture">Weimar era</a>, Berlin underwent political unrest due to economic uncertainties, but also became a renowned centre of the <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a>. The metropolis experienced its heyday as a major world capital and was known for its leadership roles in science, technology, arts, the humanities, city planning, film, higher education, government and industries. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> rose to public prominence during his years in Berlin, being awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Physics">Nobel Prize for Physics</a> in 1921.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg/220px-Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg/330px-Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg/440px-Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Potsdamer_Platz_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Berlin in ruins after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> (<a href="/wiki/Potsdamer_Platz" title="Potsdamer Platz">Potsdamer Platz</a>, 1945)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1933 <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Nazi_seizure_of_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi seizure of power">came to power</a>. NSDAP rule diminished Berlin's Jewish community from 160,000 (one-third of all Jews in the country) to about 80,000 as a result of emigration between 1933 and 1939. After <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a> in 1938, thousands of the city's Jews were imprisoned in the nearby <a href="/wiki/Sachsenhausen_concentration_camp" title="Sachsenhausen concentration camp">Sachsenhausen concentration camp</a>. Starting in early 1943, many were shipped to <a href="/wiki/Death_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Death camp">death camps</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> During World War II, large parts of Berlin were destroyed in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin_(air)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Berlin (air)">the 1943–45 air raids</a> and during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Battle of Berlin</a>. Around 125,000 civilians were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/End_of_World_War_II_in_Europe" title="End of World War II in Europe">end of the war in Europe</a> in May 1945, Berlin received large numbers of refugees from the Eastern provinces. The victorious powers divided the city into four sectors, analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">occupation zones</a> into which Germany was divided. The sectors of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a> (the United States, the United Kingdom and France) formed <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet sector</a> formed <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlinermauer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Berlinermauer.jpg/220px-Berlinermauer.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Berlinermauer.jpg/330px-Berlinermauer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Berlinermauer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlinermauer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> (painted on the western side) was a barrier that divided the city from 1961 to 1989.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All four <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> shared administrative responsibilities for Berlin. However, in 1948, when the Western Allies extended the currency reform in the Western zones of Germany to the three western sectors of Berlin, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> imposed a <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">blockade</a> on the access routes to and from West Berlin, which lay entirely inside Soviet-controlled territory. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_airlift" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin airlift">Berlin airlift</a>, conducted by the three western Allies, overcame this blockade by supplying food and other supplies to the city from June 1948 to May 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 1949 the Federal Republic of Germany was founded in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> and eventually included all of the American, British and French zones, excluding those three countries' zones in Berlin, while the <a href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist-Leninist">Marxist-Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a> was proclaimed in East Germany. West Berlin officially remained an occupied city, but it politically was aligned with the Federal Republic of Germany despite West Berlin's geographic isolation. Airline service to West Berlin was granted only to American, British and French airlines.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/220px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/330px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG/440px-Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG 2x" data-file-width="661" data-file-height="498" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thefalloftheberlinwall1989.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall#The_Fall" title="Berlin Wall">fall of the Berlin Wall</a> on 9 November 1989. On <a href="/wiki/German_Unity_Day" title="German Unity Day">3 October 1990</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> process was formally finished.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The founding of the two German states increased <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> tensions. West Berlin was surrounded by East German territory, and East Germany proclaimed the Eastern part as its capital, a move that was not recognised by the western powers. East Berlin included most of the historic centre of the city. The West German government established itself in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1961 East Germany began the building of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> between East and West Berlin, and events escalated to a tank standoff at <a href="/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie" title="Checkpoint Charlie">Checkpoint Charlie</a>. West Berlin was now de facto a part of West Germany with a unique legal status, while East Berlin was de facto a part of East Germany. <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> gave his "<i><a href="/wiki/Ich_bin_ein_Berliner" title="Ich bin ein Berliner">Ich bin ein Berliner</a></i>"&#160;–  speech in 1963 underlining the US support for the Western part of the city. Berlin was completely divided. Although it was possible for Westerners to pass from one to the other side through strictly controlled checkpoints, for most Easterners travel to West Berlin or West Germany was prohibited by the government of East Germany. In 1971, a <a href="/wiki/Four_Power_Agreement_on_Berlin" title="Four Power Agreement on Berlin">Four-Power agreement</a> guaranteed access to and from West Berlin by car or train through East Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1989, with the end of the Cold War and pressure from the East German population, the Berlin Wall fell on 9 November and was subsequently mostly demolished. Today, the <a href="/wiki/East_Side_Gallery" title="East Side Gallery">East Side Gallery</a> preserves a large portion of the wall. On 3 October 1990, the two parts of Germany were <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunified</a> as the Federal Republic of Germany and Berlin again became the official German capital. In 1991, the German Parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decision_on_the_Capital_of_Germany" title="Decision on the Capital of Germany">voted to move the seat</a> of the German capital from Bonn to Berlin, which was completed in 1999. On 18 June 1994 soldiers from the United States, France and Britain marched in a parade which was part of the ceremonies to mark the final withdrawal of foreign troops allowing a <a href="/wiki/German_reunification#Reunified_Berlin" title="German reunification">reunified Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReUnificationParade_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReUnificationParade-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Berlin%27s_2001_administrative_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin's 2001 administrative reform">Berlin's 2001 administrative reform</a> merged several districts. The number of boroughs was reduced from 23 to 12. In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Final">FIFA World Cup Final</a> was held in Berlin.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Berlin" title="Geography of Berlin">Geography of Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:665px;max-width:665px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:349px;max-width:349px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cityscape_Berlin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cityscape_Berlin.jpg/347px-Cityscape_Berlin.jpg" width="347" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cityscape_Berlin.jpg/521px-Cityscape_Berlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cityscape_Berlin.jpg/694px-Cityscape_Berlin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4496" data-file-height="2300" /></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg/220px-Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg/330px-Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg/440px-Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5313" data-file-height="3542" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_-_Aerial_view_-_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view towards northeast over central Berlin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin is situated in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, in an area of low-lying marshy woodlands with a mainly flat <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a>, part of the vast <a href="/wiki/Northern_European_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern European Plain">Northern European Plain</a> which stretches all the way from northern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to western <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. The <i>Berliner Urstromtal</i> (an ice age <a href="/wiki/Glacial_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Glacial valley">glacial valley</a>), between the low <a href="/wiki/Barnim_Plateau" title="Barnim Plateau">Barnim Plateau</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Teltow_plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Teltow plateau">Teltow Plateau</a> to the south, was formed by meltwater flowing from ice sheets at the end of the last <a href="/wiki/Weichselian_glaciation" title="Weichselian glaciation">Weichselian glaciation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spree" title="Spree">Spree</a> follows this valley now. In Spandau, a borough in the west of Berlin, the Spree empties into the river <a href="/wiki/Havel" title="Havel">Havel</a>, which flows from north to south through western Berlin. The course of the Havel is more like a chain of lakes, the largest being the Tegeler See and the <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fer_Wannsee" title="Großer Wannsee">Großer Wannsee</a>. A series of lakes also feeds into the upper Spree, which flows through the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCggelsee" title="Müggelsee">Großer Müggelsee</a> in eastern Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Substantial parts of present-day Berlin extend onto the low plateaus on both sides of the Spree Valley. Large parts of the boroughs <a href="/wiki/Reinickendorf" title="Reinickendorf">Reinickendorf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pankow" title="Pankow">Pankow</a> lie on the Barnim Plateau, while most of the boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf" title="Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf">Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steglitz-Zehlendorf" title="Steglitz-Zehlendorf">Steglitz-Zehlendorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tempelhof-Sch%C3%B6neberg" title="Tempelhof-Schöneberg">Tempelhof-Schöneberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Neuk%C3%B6lln" title="Neukölln">Neukölln</a> lie on the Teltow Plateau.</p>
<p>The borough of Spandau lies partly within the Berlin Glacial Valley and partly on the Nauen Plain, which stretches to the west of Berlin. Since 2015, the highest elevation in Berlin is found on the Arkenberge hills in Pankow, at 122 metres (400 feet). Through the dumping of construction debris, they surpassed <a href="/wiki/Teufelsberg" title="Teufelsberg">Teufelsberg</a> (120.1&#160;m or 394&#160;ft), a <a href="/wiki/Schuttberg" title="Schuttberg">hill made of rubble</a> from the ruins of the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The highest natural elevation is found on the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCggelberge" title="Müggelberge">Müggelberge</a> at 114.7 metres (376 feet), and the lowest at the Spektesee in Spandau, at 28.1 metres (92 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg/220px-Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg/330px-Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg/440px-Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="760" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luftbild_bln-schmoeckwitz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The outskirts of Berlin are covered with woodlands and numerous lakes.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Maritime temperate climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> There are significant influences of mild continental climate due to its inland position, with frosts being common in winter and there being larger temperature differences between seasons than typical for many oceanic climates. Furthermore, Berlin is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">continental climate</a> (<i>Dc</i>) under the <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate scheme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Summers are warm and sometimes humid with average high temperatures of 22–25&#160;°C (72–77&#160;°F) and lows of 12–14&#160;°C (54–57&#160;°F). Winters are cool with average high temperatures of 3&#160;°C (37&#160;°F) and lows of −2 to 0&#160;°C (28 to 32&#160;°F). Spring and autumn are generally chilly to mild. Berlin's built-up area creates a microclimate, with <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">heat stored by the city's buildings and pavement</a>. Temperatures can be 4&#160;°C (7&#160;°F) higher in the city than in the surrounding areas.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Annual precipitation is 570 millimeters (22&#160;in) with moderate rainfall throughout the year. Snowfall mainly occurs from December through March.<sup id="cite_ref-worldweather_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldweather-65">[65]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg/220px-View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg/330px-View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg/440px-View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5969" data-file-height="3040" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Park_inn_Berlin_November_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typically dense cityscape of core Berlin: <a href="/wiki/Mitte" title="Mitte">Mitte</a> area</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin's history has left the city with a <a href="/wiki/Polycentrism" title="Polycentrism">polycentric organization</a> and a highly eclectic array of architecture and buildings. The city's appearance today is predominantly shaped by the key role it played in Germany's history in the 20th century. Each of the national governments based in Berlin&#160;–  the Kingdom of Prussia, the 1871 German Empire, the Weimar Republic, Nazi Germany, East Germany, and now the reunified Germany&#160;–  initiated ambitious reconstruction programs, with each adding its own distinctive style to the city's architecture.</p>
<p>Berlin was devastated by <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Berlin_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Berlin in World War II">bombing raids</a>, fires and street battles during World War II, and many of the buildings that had remained after the war were demolished in the post-war period in both West and East Berlin. Much of this demolition was initiated by municipal architecture programs to build new residential or business quarters and main roads. Many <a href="/wiki/Ornament_(art)" title="Ornament (art)">ornaments</a> of pre-war buildings were destroyed following <a href="/wiki/Ornament_and_Crime" title="Ornament and Crime">modernist dogmas</a>. While in both systems and in reunified Berlin, various important heritage monuments were also (partly) <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_(architecture)" title="Reconstruction (architecture)">reconstructed</a>, including the <i>Forum Fridericianum</i> with e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_State_Opera" title="Berlin State Opera">State Opera</a> (1955), <a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg_Palace" title="Charlottenburg Palace">Charlottenburg Palace</a> (1957), the main monuments of the <a href="/wiki/Gendarmenmarkt" title="Gendarmenmarkt">Gendarmenmarkt</a> (1980s), <a href="/wiki/Alte_Kommandantur" title="Alte Kommandantur">Kommandantur</a> (2003) and the project to reconstruct the baroque façades of the <a href="/wiki/City_Palace,_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="City Palace, Berlin">City Palace</a>. A number of new buildings are inspired by historical predecessors or the general classical style of Berlin, such as <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Adlon" title="Hotel Adlon">Hotel Adlon</a>.</p>
<p>Clusters of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Berlin" title="List of tallest buildings in Berlin">high-rise buildings</a> emerge at disperse locations, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Potsdamer_Platz" title="Potsdamer Platz">Potsdamer Platz</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_West" title="City West">City West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alexanderplatz" title="Alexanderplatz">Alexanderplatz</a>, the latter two representing the previous centers of West and East Berlin, respectively, and the former representing the new Berlin of the 21st century built upon the previous no-man's land of the Berlin Wall. Berlin has three of the top 40 <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Germany" title="List of tallest buildings in Germany">tallest buildings</a> in Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_in_Berlin" title="Architecture in Berlin">Architecture in Berlin</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sights_in_Berlin" title="List of sights in Berlin">List of sights in Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Berlin" title="List of tallest buildings in Berlin">List of tallest buildings in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin,_Kreuzberg,_Chamissoplatz_4,_Mietshaus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg/170px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg" width="170" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg/255px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg/340px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Chamissoplatz_4%2C_Mietshaus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2923" data-file-height="2712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin,_Kreuzberg,_Chamissoplatz_4,_Mietshaus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Mixed-use_development" title="Mixed-use development">mixed-use</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a>. The 'blockrand' structure of the 1862 <a href="/wiki/Hobrecht-Plan" title="Hobrecht-Plan">Hobrecht-Plan</a> is typical for Berlin.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Berlin" title="Fernsehturm Berlin">Fernsehturm</a> (TV tower) at <a href="/wiki/Alexanderplatz" title="Alexanderplatz">Alexanderplatz</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mitte" title="Mitte">Mitte</a> is among the tallest structures in the European Union at 368&#160;m (1,207&#160;ft). Built in 1969, it is visible throughout most of the central districts of Berlin. The city can be viewed from its 204&#160;m (669&#160;ft) high observation floor. Starting here the <a href="/wiki/Karl-Marx-Allee" title="Karl-Marx-Allee">Karl-Marx-Allee</a> heads east, an avenue lined by monumental residential buildings, designed in the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Classicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist Classicism">Socialist Classicism</a> style. Adjacent to this area is the <a href="/wiki/Rotes_Rathaus" title="Rotes Rathaus">Rotes Rathaus</a> (City Hall), with its distinctive red-brick architecture. In front of it is the <a href="/wiki/Neptunbrunnen" title="Neptunbrunnen">Neptunbrunnen</a>, a fountain featuring a mythological group of <a href="/wiki/Triton_(mythology)" title="Triton (mythology)">Tritons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">personifications</a> of the four main Prussian rivers and <a href="/wiki/Neptune_(mythology)" title="Neptune (mythology)">Neptune</a> on top of it.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg/220px-Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg/330px-Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg/440px-Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brandenburger_Tor_abends.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, icon of Berlin and Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a> is an iconic landmark of Berlin and Germany; it stands as a symbol of eventful European history and of unity and peace. The <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag building</a> is the traditional seat of the German Parliament. It was remodelled by British architect <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster (architect)">Norman Foster</a> in the 1990s and features a glass dome over the session area, which allows free public access to the parliamentary proceedings and magnificent views of the city.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/East_Side_Gallery" title="East Side Gallery">East Side Gallery</a> is an open-air exhibition of art painted directly on the last existing portions of the Berlin Wall. It is the largest remaining evidence of the city's historical division.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gendarmenmarkt" title="Gendarmenmarkt">Gendarmenmarkt</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> square in Berlin, the name of which derives from the headquarters of the famous Gens d'armes regiment located here in the 18th century. It is bordered by two similarly designed cathedrals, the <a href="/wiki/Franz%C3%B6sischer_Dom" class="mw-redirect" title="Französischer Dom">Französischer Dom</a> with its observation platform and the <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Dom" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutscher Dom">Deutscher Dom</a>. The Konzerthaus (Concert Hall), home of the Berlin Symphony Orchestra, stands between the two cathedrals.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg/220px-Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg/330px-Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg/440px-Haus_der_Weltkulturen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Haus_der_Kulturen_der_Welt" title="Haus der Kulturen der Welt">Haus der Kulturen der Welt</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG/220px-Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG/330px-Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG/440px-Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin.Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe_003.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe" title="Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe">Holocaust Memorial</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_Island" title="Museum Island">Museum Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/River_Spree" class="mw-redirect" title="River Spree">River Spree</a> houses <a href="/wiki/Berlin#Museums" title="Berlin">five museums</a> built from 1830 to 1930 and is a UNESCO World Heritage site. Restoration and the construction of a main entrance to all museums, as well as the reconstruction of the <a href="/wiki/Stadtschloss,_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadtschloss, Berlin">Stadtschloss</a> is continuing.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Also located on the island and adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Lustgarten" title="Lustgarten">Lustgarten</a> and palace is <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Cathedral" title="Berlin Cathedral">Berlin Cathedral</a>, emperor William II's ambitious attempt to create a Protestant counterpart to <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a> in Rome. A large crypt houses the remains of some of the earlier Prussian royal family. <a href="/wiki/St._Hedwig%27s_Cathedral" title="St. Hedwig's Cathedral">St. Hedwig's Cathedral</a> is Berlin's Roman Catholic cathedral.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:17_20_pm_(570903628).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg/220px-17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg/330px-17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg/440px-17_20_pm_%28570903628%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:17_20_pm_(570903628).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Potsdamer Platz, Kollhoff Tower at the center and headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> to the right.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Unter_den_Linden" title="Unter den Linden">Unter den Linden</a> is a tree-lined east–west avenue from the Brandenburg Gate to the site of the former Berliner Stadtschloss, and was once Berlin's premier promenade. Many Classical buildings line the street and part of <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Humboldt University">Humboldt University</a> is located there. <a href="/wiki/Friedrichstra%C3%9Fe" title="Friedrichstraße">Friedrichstraße</a> was Berlin's legendary street during the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Twenties" title="Golden Twenties">Golden Twenties</a>. It combines 20th-century traditions with the modern architecture of today's Berlin.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg/220px-Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg/330px-Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg/440px-Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unter_den_Linden_Berlin2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Unter_den_Linden" title="Unter den Linden">Unter den Linden</a> boulevard with <a href="/wiki/Zeughaus" title="Zeughaus">Zeughaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Cathedral" title="Berlin Cathedral">Berlin Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fernsehturm_Berlin" title="Fernsehturm Berlin">Fernsehturm Berlin</a> at night.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Potsdamer_Platz" title="Potsdamer Platz">Potsdamer Platz</a> is an entire quarter built from scratch after 1995 after the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Wall</a> came down.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> To the west of Potsdamer Platz is the Kulturforum, which houses the <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie,_Berlin" title="Gemäldegalerie, Berlin">Gemäldegalerie</a>, and is flanked by the <a href="/wiki/Neue_Nationalgalerie" title="Neue Nationalgalerie">Neue Nationalgalerie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Philharmonie" title="Berliner Philharmonie">Berliner Philharmonie</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Memorial_to_the_Murdered_Jews_of_Europe" title="Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe">Memorial to the Murdered Jews of Europe</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> memorial, is situated to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area around <a href="/wiki/Hackescher_Markt" title="Hackescher Markt">Hackescher Markt</a> is home to fashionable culture, with countless clothing outlets, clubs, bars, and galleries. This includes the <a href="/wiki/Hackesche_H%C3%B6fe" title="Hackesche Höfe">Hackesche Höfe</a>, a conglomeration of buildings around several courtyards, reconstructed around 1996. The nearby <a href="/wiki/New_Synagogue,_Berlin" title="New Synagogue, Berlin">New Synagogue</a> is the center of Jewish culture.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_(Berlin)_(6340508573).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg/220px-Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg/330px-Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg/440px-Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_%28Berlin%29_%286340508573%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Le_ch%C3%A2teau_de_Charlottenburg_(Berlin)_(6340508573).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg_Palace" title="Charlottenburg Palace">Charlottenburg Palace</a> is the largest existing palace in Berlin.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Stra%C3%9Fe_des_17._Juni" title="Straße des 17. Juni">Straße des 17. Juni</a>, connecting the Brandenburg Gate and Ernst-Reuter-Platz, serves as the central east-west axis. Its name commemorates the <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_1953_in_East_Germany" title="Uprising of 1953 in East Germany">uprisings in East Berlin of 17 June 1953</a>. Approximately halfway from the Brandenburg Gate is the Großer Stern, a circular traffic island on which the <a href="/wiki/Siegess%C3%A4ule" class="mw-redirect" title="Siegessäule">Siegessäule</a> (Victory Column) is situated. This monument, built to commemorate Prussia's victories, was relocated in 1938–39 from its previous position in front of the Reichstag.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kurf%C3%BCrstendamm" title="Kurfürstendamm">Kurfürstendamm</a> is home to some of Berlin's luxurious stores with the <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Memorial_Church" title="Kaiser Wilhelm Memorial Church">Kaiser Wilhelm Memorial Church</a> at its eastern end on <a href="/wiki/Breitscheidplatz" title="Breitscheidplatz">Breitscheidplatz</a>. The church was destroyed in the Second World War and left in ruins. Nearby on Tauentzienstraße is <a href="/wiki/KaDeWe" class="mw-redirect" title="KaDeWe">KaDeWe</a>, claimed to be continental Europe's largest department store. The <a href="/wiki/Rathaus_Sch%C3%B6neberg" title="Rathaus Schöneberg">Rathaus Schöneberg</a>, where <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> made his famous "<a href="/wiki/Ich_bin_ein_Berliner" title="Ich bin ein Berliner">Ich bin ein Berliner</a>!" speech, is situated in <a href="/wiki/Tempelhof-Sch%C3%B6neberg" title="Tempelhof-Schöneberg">Tempelhof-Schöneberg</a>.</p>
<p>West of the center, <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Palace_(Germany)" title="Bellevue Palace (Germany)">Bellevue Palace</a> is the residence of the German President. <a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg_Palace" title="Charlottenburg Palace">Charlottenburg Palace</a>, which was burnt out in the Second World War, is the largest historical palace in Berlin.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Funkturm_Berlin" title="Funkturm Berlin">Funkturm Berlin</a> is a 150&#160;m (490&#160;ft) tall lattice radio tower in the fairground area, built between 1924 and 1926. It is the only observation tower which stands on insulators and has a restaurant 55&#160;m (180&#160;ft) and an observation deck 126&#160;m (413&#160;ft) above ground, which is reachable by a windowed elevator.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Oberbaumbr%C3%BCcke" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberbaumbrücke">Oberbaumbrücke</a> is Berlin's most iconic bridge, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Spree" title="Spree">River Spree</a>. It was a former East-West border crossing and connects the boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Friedrichshain" title="Friedrichshain">Friedrichshain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a>. It was completed in a <a href="/wiki/Brick_gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Brick gothic">brick gothic</a> style in 1896. The center portion has been reconstructed with a steel frame after having been destroyed in 1945. The bridge has an upper deck for the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_U-Bahn" title="Berlin U-Bahn">Berlin U-Bahn</a> line <a href="/wiki/U1_(Berlin_U-Bahn)" title="U1 (Berlin U-Bahn)">U1</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Berlin" title="Demographics of Berlin">Demographics of Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BearpitKaraoke.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/BearpitKaraoke.jpg/220px-BearpitKaraoke.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/BearpitKaraoke.jpg/330px-BearpitKaraoke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/BearpitKaraoke.jpg/440px-BearpitKaraoke.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BearpitKaraoke.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People in <a href="/wiki/Mauerpark" title="Mauerpark">Mauerpark</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 30 June 2017 the city-state of Berlin had a population of 3,690,000 registered inhabitants<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">[4]</a></sup> in an area of 891.85&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (344.35&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-statoffice_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoffice-73">[73]</a></sup> The city's population density was 4,048 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>. Berlin is the second <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_of_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities of the European Union by population within city limits">most populous city proper</a> in the EU. The <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> of Berlin comprised about 4.1 million people in 2014 in an area of 1,347&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (520&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the seventh <a href="/wiki/Largest_urban_areas_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest urban areas of the European Union">most populous urban area</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Insee_-_-_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insee_-_--5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Demographia_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demographia-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">urban agglomeration</a> of the metropolis was home to about 4.5&#160;million in an area of 5,370&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,070&#160;sq&#160;mi). As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Larger_Urban_Zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Larger Urban Zones">functional urban area</a> was home to about 5&#160;million people in an area of approximately 15,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (5,792&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The entire <a href="/wiki/Berlin/Brandenburg_Metropolitan_Region" title="Berlin/Brandenburg Metropolitan Region">Berlin-Brandenburg capital region</a> has a population of more than 6 million in an area of 30,370&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11,726&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, the city state Berlin had 37.368 live births (+6,6%), a record number since 1991. The number of deaths was 32.314. Almost 2.0 million households were counted in the city. 54 percent of them were single-person households. More than 337.000 families with children under the age of 18 lived in Berlin. In 2014 the German capital registered a migration surplus of approximately 40.000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_population2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Berlin_population2.svg/220px-Berlin_population2.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Berlin_population2.svg/330px-Berlin_population2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Berlin_population2.svg/440px-Berlin_population2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_population2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Berlin's population 1880–2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>National and international migration into the city has a long history. In 1685, following the revocation of the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Nantes" title="Edict of Nantes">Edict of Nantes</a> in France, the city responded with the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Potsdam" title="Edict of Potsdam">Edict of Potsdam</a>, which guaranteed religious freedom and tax-free status to French Huguenot refugees for ten years. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Berlin_Act" title="Greater Berlin Act">Greater Berlin Act</a> in 1920 incorporated many suburbs and surrounding cities of Berlin. It formed most of the territory that comprises modern Berlin and increased the population from 1.9&#160;million to 4&#160;million.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Active immigration and asylum politics in West Berlin triggered waves of immigration in the 1960s and 1970s. Currently, Berlin is home to about 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Germany" title="Turks in Germany">Turks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-250k_Turks_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250k_Turks-78">[78]</a></sup> making it the largest Turkish community outside of Turkey. In the 1990s the <i>Aussiedlergesetze</i> enabled immigration to Germany of some residents from the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Today ethnic <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germans_in_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Germans in Russia and the Soviet Union">Germans</a> from countries of the former Soviet Union make up the largest portion of the Russian-speaking community.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The last decade experienced an influx from various Western countries and some African regions.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> A portion of the African immigrants have settled in the <a href="/wiki/Afrikanisches_Viertel" title="Afrikanisches Viertel">Afrikanisches Viertel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Young Germans, EU-Europeans and Israelis have also settled in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
