<td>10,530</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In December 2016, there were 676,741 registered residents of foreign nationality and another 474,991 German citizens with a "migration background" <i>(Migrationshintergrund, MH)</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">[4]</a></sup> meaning they or one of their parents immigrated to Germany after 1955. Foreign residents of Berlin originate from approximately 190 different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Foreign_residents_of_Berlin_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foreign_residents_of_Berlin-84">[84]</a></sup> 48 percent of the residents under the age of 15 have migration background.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Berlin in 2009 was estimated to have 100,000 to 250,000 non-registered inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Boroughs of Berlin with a significant number of migrants or foreign born population are <a href="/wiki/Mitte_(locality)" title="Mitte (locality)">Mitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuk%C3%B6lln" title="Neukölln">Neukölln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrichshain-Kreuzberg" title="Friedrichshain-Kreuzberg">Friedrichshain-Kreuzberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are more than 20 non-indigenous communities with a population of at least 10,000 people, including <a href="/wiki/Turks_in_Berlin" title="Turks in Berlin">Turkish</a>, Polish, Russian, Lebanese, Palestinian, Serbian, Italian, Bosnian, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_community_of_Berlin" title="Vietnamese community of Berlin">Vietnamese</a>, American, Romanian, Bulgarian, Croatian, Chinese, Austrian, Ukrainian, French, British, Spanish, Israeli, Thai, Iranian, <a href="/wiki/Arabs_in_Berlin" title="Arabs in Berlin">Egyptian and Syrian communities</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlinerisch_dialect" title="Berlinerisch dialect">Berlinerisch dialect</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> is the official and predominant spoken language in Berlin. It is a <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">West Germanic language</a> that derives most of its vocabulary from the Germanic branch of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> language family. German is one of 24 languages of the European Union,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> and one of the three <a href="/wiki/Working_language" title="Working language">working languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.</p>
<p>Berlinerisch or Berlinisch is not a dialect linguistically, but has features of <a href="/wiki/Lausitzisch-neum%C3%A4rkisch_dialects" title="Lausitzisch-neumärkisch dialects">Lausitzisch-neumärkisch dialects</a>. It is spoken in Berlin and the <a href="/wiki/Berlin/Brandenburg_Metropolitan_Region" title="Berlin/Brandenburg Metropolitan Region">surrounding metropolitan area</a>. It originates from a <a href="/wiki/Mark_Brandenburgish_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Brandenburgish dialects">Mark Brandenburgish</a> variant. The dialect is now seen more as a <a href="/wiki/Sociolect" title="Sociolect">sociolect</a>, largely through increased immigration and trends among the educated population to speak <a href="/wiki/Standard_German" title="Standard German">standard German</a> in everyday life.</p>
<p>The most-commonly-spoken foreign languages in Berlin are Turkish, English, Russian, Arabic, Polish, Kurdish, Serbo-Croatian, Italian, Vietnamese, and French. Turkish, Arabic, Kurdish, Serbo-Croatian are heard more often in the western part, due to the large Middle Eastern and former-Yugoslavian communities. English, Vietnamese, Russian, and Polish have more native speakers in East Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Berlin" title="Religion in Berlin">Religion in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:DarkOrchid"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 159.78512068371px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 6.9829626776863E-13px; border-left-color:Honeydew"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Berlin (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-stats2016_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2016-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Not religious or other (75%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">EKD Protestants</a> (16.1%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> (8.9%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg/220px-141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg/330px-141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg/440px-141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4182" data-file-height="2928" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:141227_Berliner_Dom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Protestant <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Cathedral" title="Berlin Cathedral">Berlin Cathedral</a>, held by the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">EKD</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>More than 60% of Berlin residents have no registered religious affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The largest denomination in 2010 was the <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Landeskirche" title="Landeskirche">regional church body</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_of_Berlin-Brandenburg-Silesian_Upper_Lusatia" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Church of Berlin-Brandenburg-Silesian Upper Lusatia">Evangelical Church of Berlin-Brandenburg-Silesian Upper Lusatia (EKBO)</a> – a <a href="/wiki/United_church" class="mw-redirect" title="United church">United church</a>. EKBO is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany (EKD)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Union_Evangelischer_Kirchen" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Evangelischer Kirchen">Union Evangelischer Kirchen (UEK)</a>, and accounts for 18.7% of the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-kirchenmitglieder2010_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirchenmitglieder2010-92">[92]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> has 9.1% of residents registered as its members.<sup id="cite_ref-kirchenmitglieder2010_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirchenmitglieder2010-92">[92]</a></sup> About 2.7% of the population identify with other Christian denominations (mostly <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a>, but also various Protestants).<sup id="cite_ref-klStatistik2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klStatistik2010-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, an estimated 249.000 <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> resided in Berlin, making up 7.2% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> About a year later calculations based on census data for migrants from 21 countries of origin brought a similar number for Muslim migrants in Berlin (about 257,700 in May 2011). According to that 7.8% of Berlin´s 3,292,365 inhabitants were Muslim migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In 2016, the number of Muslims was estimated at about 350.000 people which portrays 9.5% of the city population.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Between 1992 and 2011 the Muslim population almost doubled.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>About 0.9% of Berliners belong to other religions. Of the estimated population of 30,000–45,000 Jewish residents,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Boston_Globe_2014-11-01_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Boston_Globe_2014-11-01-98">[98]</a></sup> approximately 12,000 are registered members of religious organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-klStatistik2010_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klStatistik2010-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Berlin is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Berlin" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Berlin">Roman Catholic archbishop of Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_of_Berlin-Brandenburg-Silesian_Upper_Lusatia" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Church of Berlin-Brandenburg-Silesian Upper Lusatia">EKBO</a>'s elected chairperson is titled the bishop of EKBO. Furthermore, Berlin is the seat of many Orthodox cathedrals, such as the Cathedral of St. Boris the Baptist, one of the two seats of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Orthodox</a> Diocese of Western and Central Europe, and the Resurrection of Christ Cathedral of the Diocese of Berlin (Patriarchate of Moscow).</p>
<p>The faithful of the different religions and denominations maintain many <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_of_worship_in_Berlin" title="List of places of worship in Berlin">places of worship in Berlin</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Independent_Evangelical_Lutheran_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent Evangelical Lutheran Church">Independent Evangelical Lutheran Church</a> has eight parishes of different sizes in Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> There are 36 <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> congregations (within <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Evangelical_Free_Church_Congregations_in_Germany" title="Union of Evangelical Free Church Congregations in Germany">Union of Evangelical Free Church Congregations in Germany</a>), 29 <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Churches</a>, 15 <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="United Methodist">United Methodist</a> churches, eight Free Evangelical Congregations, four <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Christ,_Scientist" title="Church of Christ, Scientist">Churches of Christ, Scientist</a> (1st, 2nd, 3rd, and 11th), six congregations of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Catholic">Old Catholic</a> church, and an <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> church in Berlin.</p>
<p>Berlin has more than 80 mosques,<sup id="cite_ref-Deutsche_Welle_2014-04-16_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deutsche_Welle_2014-04-16-100">[100]</a></sup> 11 synagogues, and two <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> temples, in addition to a number of <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a> groups.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Berlin" title="Politics of Berlin">Politics of Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Police" title="Berlin Police">Berlin Police</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_state">City state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: City state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg/220px-Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg/330px-Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg/440px-Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3486" data-file-height="2289" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Rotes_rathaus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rotes_Rathaus" title="Rotes Rathaus">Rotes Rathaus</a> (<i>Red City Hall</i>), seat of the Senate and Mayor of Berlin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">the reunification</a> on 3 October 1990, Berlin has been one of the three <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany#Subdivisions" title="States of Germany">city states in Germany</a> among the present 16 states of Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Abgeordnetenhaus_von_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Abgeordnetenhaus von Berlin">House of Representatives</a> (<i>Abgeordnetenhaus</i>) functions as the city and state parliament, which currently has 141 seats. Berlin's executive body is the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Berlin" title="Senate of Berlin">Senate of Berlin</a> (<i>Senat von Berlin</i>). The Senate consists of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mayors of Berlin">Governing Mayor</a> (<i>Regierender Bürgermeister</i>) and up to eight senators holding ministerial positions, one of them holding the title of "Mayor" (<i>Bürgermeister</i>) as deputy to the Governing Mayor. The total annual state budget of Berlin in 2015 exceeded €24.5 ($30.0) billion including a budget surplus of €205 ($240) million.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party</a> (SPD) and <a href="/wiki/The_Left_(Germany)" title="The Left (Germany)">The Left</a> (Die Linke) took control of the city government after the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_state_election,_2001" title="Berlin state election, 2001">2001 state election</a> and won another term in the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_state_election,_2006" title="Berlin state election, 2006">2006 state election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_state_election,_2016" title="Berlin state election, 2016">2016 state election</a>, there has been a coalition between the Social Democratic Party, the Greens and the Left Party.</p>
<p>The Governing Mayor is simultaneously Lord Mayor of the City of Berlin (<i>Oberbürgermeister der Stadt</i>) and Minister President of the Federal State of Berlin (<i>Ministerpräsident des Bundeslandes</i>). The office of the Governing Mayor is located in the <a href="/wiki/Rotes_Rathaus" title="Rotes Rathaus">Rotes Rathaus (Red City Hall)</a>. Since 2014 this office has been held by <a href="/wiki/Michael_M%C3%BCller_(politician)" title="Michael Müller (politician)">Michael Müller</a> of the Social Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs">Boroughs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Boroughs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_and_neighborhoods_of_Berlin" title="Boroughs and neighborhoods of Berlin">Boroughs and neighborhoods of Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Subdivisions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Berlin_Subdivisions.svg/280px-Berlin_Subdivisions.svg.png" width="280" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Berlin_Subdivisions.svg/420px-Berlin_Subdivisions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Berlin_Subdivisions.svg/560px-Berlin_Subdivisions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1151" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Subdivisions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boroughs_and_neighborhoods_of_Berlin" title="Boroughs and neighborhoods of Berlin">Berlin's twelve boroughs and their 96 neighborhoods</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin is subdivided into 12 boroughs or districts (<i>Bezirke</i>). Each borough is made up by a number of subdistricts or neighborhoods (<i>Ortsteile</i>), which have historic roots in much older municipalities that predate the formation of Greater Berlin on 1 October 1920. These subdistricts became urbanized and incorporated into the city later on. Many residents strongly identify with their neighbourhoods, colloquially called <i><a href="/wiki/Kiez" title="Kiez">Kiez</a></i> . At present, Berlin consists of 96 subdistricts, which are commonly made up of several smaller residential areas or quarters.</p>
<p>Each borough is governed by a borough council (<i>Bezirksamt</i>) consisting of five councilors (<i>Bezirksstadträte</i>) including the borough's mayor (<i>Bezirksbürgermeister</i>). The council is elected by the borough assembly (<i>Bezirksverordnetenversammlung</i>). However, the individual boroughs are not independent municipalities, but subordinate to the Senate of Berlin. The borough's mayors make up the council of mayors (<i>Rat der Bürgermeister</i>), which is led by the city's Governing Mayor and advises the Senate. The neighborhoods have no local government bodies.</p>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>
<p>Berlin maintains official partnerships with 17 cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Berlinsistercities_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berlinsistercities-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">Town twinning</a> between Berlin and other cities began with its sister city Los Angeles in 1967. East Berlin's partnerships were canceled at the time of German reunification but later partially reestablished. West Berlin's partnerships had previously been restricted to the borough level. During the Cold War era, the partnerships had reflected the different power blocs, with West Berlin partnering with capitals in the Western World, and East Berlin mostly partnering with cities from the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> and its allies.</p>
<p>There are several joint projects with many other cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. Berlin participates in international city associations such as the Union of the Capitals of the European Union, Eurocities, Network of European Cities of Culture, Metropolis, Summit Conference of the World's Major Cities, and Conference of the World's Capital Cities. Berlin's official sister cities are:<sup id="cite_ref-Berlinsistercities_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berlinsistercities-104">[104]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_city">Capital city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Capital city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Berlin is the capital of the Federal Republic of Germany. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Germany" title="President of Germany">President of Germany</a>, whose functions are mainly ceremonial under the <a href="/wiki/Grundgesetz" class="mw-redirect" title="Grundgesetz">German constitution</a>, has their official residence in <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Palace_(Germany)" title="Bellevue Palace (Germany)">Bellevue Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Berlin is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic_of_Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic of Germany)">German executive</a>, housed in the <a href="/wiki/German_Chancellery" title="German Chancellery">Chancellery</a>, the <i>Bundeskanzleramt</i>. Facing the Chancellery is the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a>, the German Parliament, housed in the renovated <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag building</a> since the government's relocation to Berlin in 1998. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesrat_of_Germany" title="Bundesrat of Germany">Bundesrat</a> ("federal council", performing the function of an upper house) is the representation of the Federal States (<i>Bundesländer</i>) of Germany and has its seat at the former <a href="/wiki/Prussian_House_of_Lords" title="Prussian House of Lords">Prussian House of Lords</a>. The total annual federal budget managed by the German government exceeded €310 ($375) billion in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

<p>The relocation of the federal <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Germany" title="Cabinet of Germany">government</a> and Bundestag to Berlin was mostly completed in 1999, however some ministries as well as some minor departments stayed in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_city" title="Federal city">federal city</a> <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, the former capital of West Germany. <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Bonn_Act" title="Berlin-Bonn Act">Discussions about moving</a> the remaining ministries and departments to Berlin continue.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The ministries and departments of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Defence_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Defence (Germany)">Defence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Justice_and_Consumer_Protection" title="Federal Ministry of Justice and Consumer Protection">Justice and Consumer Protection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Finance_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Finance (Germany)">Finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_the_Interior_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of the Interior (Germany)">Interior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Office_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Office (Germany)">Foreign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_for_Economic_Affairs_and_Energy_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Ministry for Economic Affairs and Energy (Germany)">Economic Affairs and Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Labour_and_Social_Affairs" title="Federal Ministry of Labour and Social Affairs">Labour and Social Affairs</a> , <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Family_Affairs,_Senior_Citizens,_Women_and_Youth" title="Federal Ministry of Family Affairs, Senior Citizens, Women and Youth">Family Affairs, Senior Citizens, Women and Youth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_for_the_Environment,_Nature_Conservation,_Building_and_Nuclear_Safety" title="Federal Ministry for the Environment, Nature Conservation, Building and Nuclear Safety">Environment, Nature Conservation, Building and Nuclear Safety</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Food_and_Agriculture" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Ministry of Food and Agriculture">Food and Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_for_Economic_Cooperation_and_Development" title="Federal Ministry for Economic Cooperation and Development">Economic Cooperation and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Health_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Health (Germany)">Health</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Transport_and_Digital_Infrastructure" title="Federal Ministry of Transport and Digital Infrastructure">Transport and Digital Infrastructure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Education_and_Research_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Education and Research (Germany)">Education and Research</a> are based in the capital.</p>
<p>Berlin hosts in total 158 foreign embassies<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> as well as the headquarters of many think tanks, trade unions, non-profit organizations, lobbying groups, and professional associations. Due to the influence and international partnerships of the Federal Republic of Germany, the capital city has become a significant centre of German and European affairs. Frequent official visits, and diplomatic consultations among governmental representatives and national leaders are common in contemporary Berlin.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Berlin" title="Economy of Berlin">Economy of Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg/220px-Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg/330px-Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg/440px-Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Panorama_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Berlin is a UNESCO "City of Design" and recognized for its <a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">creative industries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Startup_ecosystem" title="Startup ecosystem">startup ecosystem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2015 the nominal GDP of the citystate Berlin totaled €124.16 (~$142) billion compared to €117.75 in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> an increase of about 5.4%. Berlin's economy is dominated by the service sector, with around 84% of all companies doing business in services. In 2015, the total labour force in Berlin was 1.85 million. The unemployment rate reached a 24-year low in November 2015 and stood at 10.0% .<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> From 2012–2015 Berlin, as a German state, had the highest annual employment growth rate. Around 130,000 jobs were added in this period.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Important economic sectors in Berlin include life sciences, transportation, information and communication technologies, media and music, advertising and design, biotechnology, environmental services, construction, e-commerce, retail, hotel business, and medical engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research and development have economic significance for the city.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> Several major corporations like Volkswagen, Pfizer, and SAP operate innovation laboratories in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The Science and Business Park in Adlershof is the largest technology park in Germany measured by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Within the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, Berlin has become a center for business relocation and international <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">investments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Companies">Companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg/220px-2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg/330px-2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg/440px-2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4669" data-file-height="3113" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2015-03-22_D-ABKT_at_Berlin-Tegel_TXL_by_sebaso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> is headquartered in Berlin.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many German and international companies have business or service centers in the city. For several years Berlin has been recognized as a major center of <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">business founders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In 2015 Berlin generated the most venture capital for young <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup companies</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the 10 largest employers in Berlin are the City-State of Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>, the hospital provider <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charité">Charité</a> and Vivantes, the Federal Government of Germany, the local public transport provider <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Verkehrsbetriebe" title="Berliner Verkehrsbetriebe">BVG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a>. The two largest banks headquartered in the capital are <i>Investitionsbank Berlin</i> and <a href="/wiki/Landesbank_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Landesbank Berlin">Landesbank Berlin</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler</a> manufactures cars, and <a href="/wiki/BMW_Motorrad" title="BMW Motorrad">BMW builds motorcycles</a> in Berlin. <a href="/wiki/Bayer_Schering_Pharma" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayer Schering Pharma">Bayer Health Care</a> and <i>Berlin Chemie</i> are major pharmaceutical companies in the city. The second largest German airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> is based there as well.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Global 500</a> and <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a>-listed company is partly headquartered in Berlin. The national railway operator <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>, the <a href="/wiki/MDAX" title="MDAX">MDAX</a>-listed firms <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Springer AG">Axel Springer SE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zalando" title="Zalando">Zalando</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/SDAX" title="SDAX">SDAX</a> listed company <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Internet" title="Rocket Internet">Rocket Internet</a> have their main headquarters in the central districts.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Among the largest international corporations who operate a German or European headquarter in Berlin are <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier Transportation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazprom_Germania" title="Gazprom Germania">Gazprom Germania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">Total S.A.</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_and_conventions">Tourism and conventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism and conventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sights_in_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Sights in Berlin">Sights in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:420px;max-width:420px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:208px;max-width:208px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg/206px-Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg" width="206" height="137" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg/309px-Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg/412px-Berlin_Fashion_Week_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Fashion_Week" title="Berlin Fashion Week">Berlin Fashion Week</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:208px;max-width:208px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG/206px-IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG" width="206" height="137" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG/309px-IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG/412px-IFA_2012_IMG_7677.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Internationale_Funkausstellung_Berlin" title="Internationale Funkausstellung Berlin">IFA</a> is the world's leading trade show for consumer electronics.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin had 788 hotels with 134,399 beds in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-visitberlin_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitberlin-125">[125]</a></sup> The city recorded 28.7&#160;million overnight hotel stays and 11.9&#160;million hotel guests in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-visitberlin_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitberlin-125">[125]</a></sup> Tourism figures have more than doubled within the last ten years and Berlin has become the third most-visited city destination in Europe. The largest visitor groups are from Germany, the United Kingdom, the Netherlands, Italy, Spain and the United States.</p>
<p>According to figures from the <a href="/wiki/International_Congress_and_Convention_Association" title="International Congress and Convention Association">International Congress and Convention Association</a> in 2015 Berlin became the leading organizer of conferences in the world hosting 195 international meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Some of these congress events take place on venues such as CityCube Berlin or the Berlin Congress Center (bcc).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Messe_Berlin" title="Messe Berlin">Messe Berlin</a> (also known as Berlin ExpoCenter City) is the main convention organizing company in the city. Its main exhibition area covers more than 160,000 square metres (1,722,226 square feet). Several large-scale trade fairs like the consumer electronics trade fair <a href="/wiki/IFA_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="IFA Berlin">IFA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/ILA_Berlin_Air_Show" title="ILA Berlin Air Show">ILA Berlin Air Show</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Fashion_Week" title="Berlin Fashion Week">Berlin Fashion Week</a> (including the <i>Premium Berlin</i> and the <i>Panorama Berlin</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Green_Week" title="Berlin International Green Week">Green Week</a>, the <i>Fruit Logistica</i>, the transport fair <a href="/wiki/InnoTrans" title="InnoTrans">InnoTrans</a>, the tourism fair <a href="/wiki/ITB_Berlin" title="ITB Berlin">ITB</a> and the adult entertainment and erotic fair <a href="/wiki/Venus_Award" title="Venus Award">Venus</a> are held annually in the city, attracting a significant number of business visitors.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_industries">Creative industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Creative industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_Berlin" title="List of films set in Berlin">List of films set in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg/220px-European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg/330px-European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg/440px-European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="150" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Film_Academy_-_European_Film_Awards_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/European_Film_Academy" title="European Film Academy">European Film Academy</a> (logo pictured) was founded in Berlin.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">creative arts and entertainment</a> business is an important and sizable sector of the economy of Berlin. The sector comprises music, film, advertising, architecture, art, design, <a href="/wiki/German_fashion" title="German fashion">fashion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a>, publishing, <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">R&amp;D</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> TV, radio, and <a href="/wiki/Video_gaming_in_Germany" title="Video gaming in Germany">video games</a>.</p>
<p>In 2014 around 30,500 creative companies were operating in the Berlin-Brandenburg metropolitan region, predominantly <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium-sized_enterprises" title="Small and medium-sized enterprises">SMEs</a>. Generating a revenue of 15.6 billion Euro and 6% of all private economic sales, the culture industry grew from 2009 to 2014 at an average rate of 5.5% per year.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Berlin is an important centre in the European and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Germany" title="Cinema of Germany">German film industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> It is home to more than 1,000 film and television production companies, 270 movie theaters, and around 300 national and international co-productions are filmed in the region every year.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> The historic <a href="/wiki/Babelsberg_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Babelsberg Studios">Babelsberg Studios</a> and the production company <a href="/wiki/Universum_Film_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Universum Film AG">UFA</a> are located adjacent to Berlin in <a href="/wiki/Potsdam" title="Potsdam">Potsdam</a>. The city is also home of the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Filmakademie" title="Deutsche Filmakademie">German Film Academy</a> (Deutsche Filmakademie), founded in 2003, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Film_Academy" title="European Film Academy">European Film Academy</a>, founded in 1988.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Berlin" title="Media in Berlin">Media in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin,_Kreuzberg,_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse,_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg/170px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg" width="170" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg/255px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg/340px-Berlin%2C_Kreuzberg%2C_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse%2C_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3103" data-file-height="2966" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin,_Kreuzberg,_Rudi-Dutschke-Strasse,_Axel-Springer-Hochhaus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Headquarter of the <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Springer AG">Axel Springer SE</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin is home to numerous magazine, newspaper, book and scientific/academic publishers, as well as their associated service industries. In addition around 20 news agencies, more than 90 regional daily newspapers and their websites, as well as the Berlin offices of more than 22 national publications such as <a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a> re-enforce the capital's position as Germany's epicenter for influential debate. Therefore, many international journalists, bloggers and writers live and work in the city.</p>
<p>Berlin is the central location to several international and regional television and radio stations.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Rundfunk_Berlin-Brandenburg" title="Rundfunk Berlin-Brandenburg">RBB</a> has its headquarters in Berlin as well as the commercial broadcasters <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe" title="MTV Europe">MTV Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viva_(TV_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Viva (TV station)">VIVA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/N24_(Germany)" title="N24 (Germany)">N24</a>. German international public broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a> has its TV production unit in Berlin, and most national German broadcasters have a studio in the city including <a href="/wiki/ZDF" title="ZDF">ZDF</a> and <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" title="RTL Television">RTL</a>.</p>
<p>Berlin has Germany's largest number of daily newspapers, with numerous local <a href="/wiki/Broadsheet" title="Broadsheet">broadsheets</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Berliner_Morgenpost" title="Berliner Morgenpost">Berliner Morgenpost</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Berliner_Zeitung" title="Berliner Zeitung">Berliner Zeitung</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Tagesspiegel" title="Der Tagesspiegel">Der Tagesspiegel</a></i>), and three major <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloids</a>, as well as national dailies of varying sizes, each with a different political affiliation, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Welt" title="Die Welt">Die Welt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Neues_Deutschland" title="Neues Deutschland">Neues Deutschland</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Tageszeitung" title="Die Tageszeitung">Die Tageszeitung</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Exberliner" title="Exberliner">Exberliner</a></i>, a monthly magazine, is Berlin's English-language periodical and <a href="/wiki/La_Gazette_de_Berlin" title="La Gazette de Berlin">La Gazette de Berlin</a> a French-language newspaper.</p>
<p>Berlin is also the headquarter of major German-language <a href="/wiki/Publishing_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Publishing house">publishing houses</a> like <a href="/wiki/Walter_de_Gruyter" title="Walter de Gruyter">Walter de Gruyter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Springer AG">Springer</a>, the Ullstein Verlagsgruppe (publishing group), <a href="/wiki/Suhrkamp" class="mw-redirect" title="Suhrkamp">Suhrkamp</a> and Cornelsen are all based in Berlin. Each of which publish books, periodicals, and multimedia products.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Berlin" title="Transport in Berlin">Transport in Berlin</a></div>
<dl>
<dt>Road</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg/220px-Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg/330px-Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg/440px-Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_hauptbahnhof_no_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hauptbahnhof" title="Berlin Hauptbahnhof">Berlin Hauptbahnhof</a> is the largest grade-separated railway station in Europe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin's transport infrastructure is highly complex, providing a diverse range of urban mobility.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> A total of 979 bridges cross 197&#160;km (122&#160;mi) of inner-city waterways. 5,422&#160;km (3,369&#160;mi) of roads run through Berlin, of which 77&#160;km (48&#160;mi) are motorways ("<a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2013, 1.344&#160;million motor vehicles were registered in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics-133">[133]</a></sup> With 377 cars per 1000 residents in 2013 (570/1000 in Germany), Berlin as a <a href="/wiki/Western_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Western World">Western</a> global city has one of the lowest numbers of cars per capita. In 2012 around 7600 mostly beige colored <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicabs</a> were in service. Since 2011 a number of app based <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">e-car</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">e-scooter</a> sharing services have evolved.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Rail</dt>
</dl>
<p>Long-distance rail lines connect Berlin with all of the major cities of Germany and with many cities in neighboring European countries. Regional rail lines of the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Berlin-Brandenburg" title="Verkehrsverbund Berlin-Brandenburg">Verkehrsverbund Berlin-Brandenburg</a> provide access to the surrounding regions of Brandenburg and to the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hauptbahnhof" title="Berlin Hauptbahnhof">Berlin Hauptbahnhof</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade-separated</a> <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway station</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> runs high speed <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE trains</a> to domestic destinations like <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> and others. It also runs an SXF airport express rail service, as well as trains to several international destinations like <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Public transport</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Berliner_Verkehrsbetriebe" title="Berliner Verkehrsbetriebe">Berliner Verkehrsbetriebe</a></span> and the Deutsche Bahn manage several extensive urban public transport systems.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
