<dl>
<dt>Airports</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BER-Destinations.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BER-Destinations.png/220px-BER-Destinations.png" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BER-Destinations.png/330px-BER-Destinations.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/BER-Destinations.png/440px-BER-Destinations.png 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1766" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BER-Destinations.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flights departing from Berlin serve 163 destinations around the globe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has two commercial international airports. <a href="/wiki/Tegel_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Tegel Airport">Tegel Airport</a> (TXL) is situated within the city limits. <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Schönefeld Airport">Schönefeld Airport</a> (SXF) is located just outside Berlin's south-eastern border in the state of Brandenburg. Both airports together handled 29.5 million passengers in 2015. In 2014, 67 airlines served 163 destinations in 50 countries from Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Tegel Airport is an important transfer hub for <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> as well as a focus city for <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>. Schönefeld serves as an important destination for airlines like <a href="/wiki/Germania_(airline)" title="Germania (airline)">Germania</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.</p>
<p>The new <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a> (BER), currently under construction, will replace Tegel as single commercial airport of Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The airport is going to integrate Schönefeld (SXF) facilities and is estimated to open in October 2019. The BER will have an initial capacity of around 35 million passengers per year. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, plans for further expansion bringing the terminal capacity to approximately 50 million per year are in development.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Cycling</dt>
</dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_Berlin" title="Cycling in Berlin">Cycling in Berlin</a></div>
<p>Berlin is well known for its highly developed bicycle lane system.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> It is estimated that Berlin has 710 bicycles per 1000 residents. Around 500,000 daily bike riders accounted for 13% of total traffic in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Cyclists have access to 620&#160;km (385&#160;mi) of bicycle paths including approximately 150&#160;km (93&#160;mi) of mandatory bicycle paths, 190&#160;km (118&#160;mi) of off-road bicycle routes, 60&#160;km (37&#160;mi) of bicycle lanes on roads, 70&#160;km (43&#160;mi) of shared bus lanes which are also open to cyclists, 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) of combined pedestrian/bike paths and 50&#160;km (31&#160;mi) of marked bicycle lanes on roadside pavements (or sidewalks).<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Riders are allowed to carry their bicycles on <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">Regionalbahn</a>, S-Bahn and U-Bahn trains, on trams, and on night buses if a bike ticket is purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg/220px-Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg/330px-Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg/440px-Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin-mitte_heizkraftwerk-mitte_20060605_629.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Power plant Heizkraftwerk Mitte</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin's two largest energy provider for private households are the Swedish firm <a href="/wiki/Vattenfall" title="Vattenfall">Vattenfall</a> and the Berlin-based company <a href="/wiki/GASAG" title="GASAG">GASAG</a>. Both offer electric power and natural gas supply. Some of the city´s electric energy is imported from nearby power plants in southern <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the five <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Germany" title="List of power stations in Germany">largest power plants measured by capacity</a> are the Heizkraftwerk Reuter West, the Heizkraftwerk Lichterfelde, the Heizkraftwerk Mitte, the Heizkraftwerk Wilmersdorf, and the Heizkraftwerk Charlottenburg. All of these <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power stations</a> generate <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heat" title="Heat">useful heat</a> at the same time to facilitate buffering during load peaks.</p>
<p>In 1993 the power grid connections in the Berlin-Brandenburg capital region were renewed. In most of the inner districts of Berlin power lines are underground cables; only a 380&#160;kV and a 110&#160;kV line, which run from Reuter substation to the urban <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a>, use overhead lines. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_380-kV_electric_line" title="Berlin 380-kV electric line">Berlin 380-kV electric line</a> is the backbone of the city's energy grid.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg/220px-2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg/330px-2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg/440px-2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="930" data-file-height="532" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2016_Charite_Hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charité">Charité</a> university hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has a long history of discoveries in medicine and innovations in medical technology.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The modern history of medicine has been significantly influenced by scientists from Berlin. <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Virchow" title="Rudolf Virchow">Rudolf Virchow</a> was the founder of cellular pathology, while <a href="/wiki/Robert_Koch" title="Robert Koch">Robert Koch</a> developed vaccines for anthrax, cholera, and tuberculosis.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charité">Charité</a> complex (Universitätsklinik Charité) is the largest <a href="/wiki/University_hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="University hospital">university hospital</a> in Europe, tracing back its origins to the year 1710. The Charité is spread over four sites and comprises 3,300 beds, around 14,000 staff, 7,000 students, and more than 60 operating theaters, and it has a turnover of over one billion euros annually. The <a href="/wiki/Charit%C3%A9" title="Charité">Charité</a> is a joint institution of the <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Berlin" title="Free University of Berlin">Freie Universität Berlin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a>, including a wide range of institutes and specialized medical centers.</p>
<p>Among them are the German Heart Center, one of the most renowned transplantation centers, the Max-Delbrück-Center for Molecular Medicine and the Max-Planck-Institute for Molecular Genetics. The scientific research at these institutions is complemented by many research departments of companies such as Siemens and Bayer. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Summit" title="World Health Summit">World Health Summit</a> and several international health related conventions are held annually in Berlin.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunication">Telecommunication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Telecommunication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_oberholz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/St_oberholz.jpg/220px-St_oberholz.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/St_oberholz.jpg/330px-St_oberholz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/St_oberholz.jpg/440px-St_oberholz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_oberholz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students at the St. Oberholz café in Berlin Mitte using <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> devices</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital television</a> standard in Berlin and Germany is <a href="/wiki/DVB-T" title="DVB-T">DVB-T</a>. This system transmits <a href="/wiki/Video_compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Video compression">compressed</a> <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio" title="Digital audio">digital audio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">digital video</a> and other data in an <a href="/wiki/MPEG_transport_stream" title="MPEG transport stream">MPEG transport stream</a>. The transmission standard is scheduled to be replaced by <a href="/wiki/DVB-T2" title="DVB-T2">DVB-T2</a> in 2017.</p>
<p>Berlin has installed several hundred free public <a href="/wiki/Wireless_LAN" title="Wireless LAN">Wireless LAN</a> sites across the capital since 2016. The wireless networks are concentrated mostly in central districts; 650 hotspots (325 indoor and 325 outdoor access points) are installed.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Deutsche Bahn is planning to introduce Wi-Fi services in long distance and regional trains in 2017.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/UMTS" title="UMTS">UMTS</a> (3G) and <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> (4G) networks of the three major cellular operators <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a>, <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica_Germany" title="Telefónica Germany">O2</a> enable the use of mobile broadband applications citywide.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Institute_for_Telecommunications" title="Fraunhofer Institute for Telecommunications">Fraunhofer Heinrich Hertz Institute</a> develops mobile and stationary <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a> communication networks and multimedia systems. Focal points are <a href="/wiki/Photonics" title="Photonics">photonic components and systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">fiber optic</a> sensor systems, and <a href="/wiki/Digital_image_processing" title="Digital image processing">image signal processing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Signal_processing" title="Signal processing">transmission</a>. Future applications for broadband networks are developed as well.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Berlin" title="Education in Berlin">Education in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt_monument.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Humboldt_monument.jpg/170px-Humboldt_monument.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Humboldt_monument.jpg/255px-Humboldt_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Humboldt_monument.jpg/340px-Humboldt_monument.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt_monument.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a>. 40 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation#Humboldt_University_Berlin_.2813th.29" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel Prize winners</a> are affiliated with the Berlin-based colleges.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has 878 schools that teach 340,658 children in 13,727 classes and 56,787 trainees in businesses and elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> The city has a 6-year primary education program. After completing primary school, students continue to the Sekundarschule (a comprehensive school) or Gymnasium (college preparatory school). Berlin has a special bilingual school program embedded in the "Europaschule" in which children are taught the curriculum in German and a foreign language, starting in primary school and continuing in high school. Nine major European languages can be chosen as foreign languages in 29 schools.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Franz%C3%B6sisches_Gymnasium_Berlin" title="Französisches Gymnasium Berlin">Französisches Gymnasium Berlin</a>, which was founded in 1689 to teach the children of Huguenot refugees, offers (German/French) instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_School,_Berlin" title="John F. Kennedy School, Berlin">John F. Kennedy School</a>, a bilingual German–American public school located in <a href="/wiki/Zehlendorf_(Berlin)" title="Zehlendorf (Berlin)">Zehlendorf</a>, is particularly popular with children of diplomats and the English-speaking expatriate community. Four schools teach <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_Greek" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical Greek">Classical Greek</a>. Two of them are state schools (Steglitzer Gymnasium in <a href="/wiki/Steglitz" title="Steglitz">Steglitz</a> and Goethe-Gymnasium in <a href="/wiki/Wilmersdorf" title="Wilmersdorf">Wilmersdorf</a>), one is Protestant (<a href="/wiki/Evangelisches_Gymnasium_zum_Grauen_Kloster" title="Evangelisches Gymnasium zum Grauen Kloster">Evangelisches Gymnasium zum Grauen Kloster</a> in Wilmersdorf), and one is Jesuit (<a href="/wiki/Canisius-Kolleg" class="mw-redirect" title="Canisius-Kolleg">Canisius-Kolleg</a> in the "Embassy Quarter" in <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten_(Berlin)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiergarten (Berlin)">Tiergarten</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Universities_and_research_institutions_in_Berlin" title="Universities and research institutions in Berlin">Universities and research institutions in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg/260px-Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg" width="260" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg/390px-Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg/520px-Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1279" data-file-height="555" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Freie_Universitaet_Berlin_-_Gebaeudekomplex_Rost-_und_Silberlaube.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Berlin" title="Free University of Berlin">Free University</a> is one of Germany's eleven "Universities of Excellence".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Berlin-Brandenburg capital region is one of the most prolific centres of higher education and research in Germany and Europe. Historically, 40 Nobel Prize winners are affiliated with the Berlin-based universities.</p>
<p>The city has four public research universities and more than 30 private, professional, and technical colleges <i>(Hochschulen)</i>, offering a wide range of disciplines.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> A record number of 175,651 students were enrolled in the winter term of 2015/16.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Among them around 18% have an international background.</p>
<p>The three largest universities combined have approximately 100,000 enrolled students. There are the <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt Universität zu Berlin</a> <i>(HU Berlin)</i> with 33,000 students, the <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Berlin" title="Free University of Berlin">Freie Universität Berlin</a> <i>(Free University of Berlin, FU Berlin)</i> with about 33,000 students, and the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Berlin" title="Technical University of Berlin">Technische Universität Berlin</a> <i>(TU Berlin)</i> with 33,000 students. The FU and the HU are part of the <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">German Universities Excellence Initiative</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_University_of_the_Arts" title="Berlin University of the Arts">Universität der Künste</a> <i>(UdK)</i> has about 4,000 students. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_School_of_Economics_and_Law" title="Berlin School of Economics and Law">Berlin School of Economics and Law</a> has an enrollment of about 10,000 students and the <a href="/wiki/HTW_Berlin" title="HTW Berlin">Hochschule für Technik und Wirtschaft</a> (University of Applied Sciences for Engineering and Economics) of about 13.000 students.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg/220px-Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg/330px-Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg/440px-Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1798" data-file-height="1199" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Adlershof_Photonics_Center_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/WISTA" title="WISTA">Science and Technology Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Adlershof" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Adlershof">Adlershof</a> is home to several new businesses and research institutes.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has a high density of internationally renowned research institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Leibniz_Association" title="Leibniz Association">Leibniz Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz_Association_of_German_Research_Centres" title="Helmholtz Association of German Research Centres">Helmholtz Association</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a>, which are independent of, or only loosely connected to its universities.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2012, around 65,000 professional scientists were working in <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Berlin is one of the knowledge and innovation communities (KIC) of the <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_of_Innovation_and_Technology" title="European Institute of Innovation and Technology">European Institute of Innovation and Technology</a> (EIT).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> The KIC is based at the Centre for Entrepreneurship at TU Berlin and has a focus in the development of IT industries. It partners with major multinational companies such as Siemens, Deutsche Telekom, and SAP.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of Europe's successful research, business and technology <a href="/wiki/List_of_technology_centers" title="List of technology centers">clusters</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/WISTA" title="WISTA">WISTA</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berlin-Adlershof" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin-Adlershof">Berlin-Adlershof</a>, with more than 1,000 affiliated firms, university departments and scientific institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the libraries that are affiliated with the various universities, the <a href="/wiki/Staatsbibliothek_zu_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin">Staatsbibliothek zu Berlin</a> is a major research library. Its two main locations are on Potsdamer Straße and on <a href="/wiki/Unter_den_Linden" title="Unter den Linden">Unter den Linden</a>. There are also 86 public libraries in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ResearchGate" title="ResearchGate">ResearchGate</a>, a global social networking site for scientists, is based in Berlin.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_in_Berlin" title="Culture in Berlin">Culture in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:403px;max-width:403px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:197px;max-width:197px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_(Zuschnitt).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/195px-Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg" width="195" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/293px-Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/390px-Alte_Nationalgalerie_abends_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4674" data-file-height="3216" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Alte_Nationalgalerie" title="Alte Nationalgalerie">Alte Nationalgalerie</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Island" title="Museum Island">Museum Island</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG/200px-20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG/300px-20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG/400px-20150208_-_Berlinale_Palast_and_Red_Carpet.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Berlinale" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlinale">Berlinale</a> is the largest international spectator film festival.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin is known for its numerous cultural institutions, many of which enjoy international reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO2_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO2-154">[154]</a></sup> The diversity and vivacity of the metropolis led to a trendsetting atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> An innovative music, dance and art scene has developed in the 21st century.</p>
<p>Young people, international artists and entrepreneurs continued to settle in the city and made Berlin a popular entertainment center in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>The expanding cultural performance of the city was underscored by the relocation of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> who decided to move their headquarters to the banks of the River Spree.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In 2005, Berlin was named "City of Design" by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cityofdesign_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cityofdesign-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galleries_and_museums">Galleries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Galleries and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_and_galleries_in_Berlin" title="List of museums and galleries in Berlin">List of museums and galleries in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg/170px-Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg/255px-Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg/340px-Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jewishmuseumberlin2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Museum Berlin">Jewish Museum</a> presents two millennia of <a href="/wiki/German_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="German Jews">German–Jewish history</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Berlin is home to 138 museums and more than 400 art galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The ensemble on the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Island" title="Museum Island">Museum Island</a> is a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> and is situated in the northern part of the Spree Island between the Spree and the Kupfergraben.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-22">[22]</a></sup> As early as 1841 it was designated a "district dedicated to art and antiquities" by a royal decree. Subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/Altes_Museum" title="Altes Museum">Altes Museum</a> was built in the Lustgarten. The <a href="/wiki/Neues_Museum" title="Neues Museum">Neues Museum</a>, which displays the <a href="/wiki/Nefertiti_Bust" title="Nefertiti Bust">bust of Queen Nefertiti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alte_Nationalgalerie" title="Alte Nationalgalerie">Alte Nationalgalerie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pergamon_Museum" title="Pergamon Museum">Pergamon Museum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bode_Museum" title="Bode Museum">Bode Museum</a> were built there.</p>
<p>Apart from the Museum Island, there are many additional museums in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie,_Berlin" title="Gemäldegalerie, Berlin">Gemäldegalerie</a> (Painting Gallery) focuses on the paintings of the "old masters" from the 13th to the 18th centuries, while the <a href="/wiki/Neue_Nationalgalerie" title="Neue Nationalgalerie">Neue Nationalgalerie</a> (New National Gallery, built by <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Mies_van_der_Rohe" title="Ludwig Mies van der Rohe">Ludwig Mies van der Rohe</a>) specializes in 20th-century European painting. The <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Bahnhof" title="Hamburger Bahnhof">Hamburger Bahnhof</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Moabit" title="Moabit">Moabit</a>, exhibits a major collection of modern and contemporary art. The expanded <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Historisches_Museum" title="Deutsches Historisches Museum">Deutsches Historisches Museum</a> re-opened in the Zeughaus with an overview of German history spanning more than a millennium. The <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus_Archive" title="Bauhaus Archive">Bauhaus Archive</a> is a museum of 20th century design from the famous <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">Bauhaus</a> school.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg/220px-Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg/330px-Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg/440px-Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ishtar_Gate_at_Berlin_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The reconstructed <a href="/wiki/Ishtar_Gate" title="Ishtar Gate">Ishtar Gate</a> of Babylon at the <a href="/wiki/Pergamon_Museum" title="Pergamon Museum">Pergamon Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Museum Berlin">Jewish Museum</a> has a standing exhibition on two millennia of German-Jewish history.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/German_Museum_of_Technology_(Berlin)" class="mw-redirect" title="German Museum of Technology (Berlin)">German Museum of Technology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a> has a large collection of historical technical artifacts. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Naturkunde" title="Museum für Naturkunde">Museum für Naturkunde</a> exhibits natural history near <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Hauptbahnhof" title="Berlin Hauptbahnhof">Berlin Hauptbahnhof</a>. It has the largest mounted dinosaur in the world (a <a href="/wiki/Giraffatitan" title="Giraffatitan">Giraffatitan</a>). Well-preserved specimens of <a href="/wiki/Tyrannosaurus_Rex" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyrannosaurus Rex">Tyrannosaurus Rex</a> and the early bird <a href="/wiki/Archaeopteryx" title="Archaeopteryx">Archaeopteryx</a> are at display as well.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Dahlem_(Berlin)" title="Dahlem (Berlin)">Dahlem</a>, there are several museums of world art and culture, such as the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Asian_Art" title="Museum of Asian Art">Museum of Asian Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ethnological_Museum_of_Berlin" title="Ethnological Museum of Berlin">Ethnological Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Europ%C3%A4ischer_Kulturen" title="Museum Europäischer Kulturen">Museum of European Cultures</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Museum" title="Allied Museum">Allied Museum</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCcke_Museum" title="Brücke Museum">Brücke Museum</a> features one of the largest collection of works by artist of the early 20th-century expressionist movement. In <a href="/wiki/Lichtenberg" title="Lichtenberg">Lichtenberg</a>, on the grounds of the former <a href="/wiki/Stasi" title="Stasi">East German Ministry for State Security</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Stasi_Museum" title="Stasi Museum">Stasi Museum</a>. The site of <a href="/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie" title="Checkpoint Charlie">Checkpoint Charlie</a>, one of the most renowned crossing points of the Berlin Wall, is still preserved. A private <a href="/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie_Museum" title="Checkpoint Charlie Museum">museum venture</a> exhibits a comprehensive documentation of detailed plans and strategies devised by people who tried to flee from the East. The <a href="/wiki/Beate_Uhse_Erotic_Museum" title="Beate Uhse Erotic Museum">Beate Uhse Erotic Museum</a> claims to be the world's largest erotic museum.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cityscape of Berlin displays large quantities of urban <a href="/wiki/Street_art" title="Street art">street art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> It has become a significant part of the city's cultural heritage and has its roots in the graffiti scene of <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a> of the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall_graffiti_art" title="Berlin Wall graffiti art">Berlin Wall</a> itself has become one of the largest open-air canvasses in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The leftover stretch along the Spree river in <a href="/wiki/Friedrichshain" title="Friedrichshain">Friedrichshain</a> remains as the <a href="/wiki/East_Side_Gallery" title="East Side Gallery">East Side Gallery</a>. Berlin today is consistently rated as an important world city for street art culture.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife_and_festivals">Nightlife and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Nightlife and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg/170px-Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg/255px-Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg/340px-Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franzoesischer_Dom_-_Festival_of_Lights_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/French_Cathedral,_Berlin" title="French Cathedral, Berlin">French Cathedral</a> during the annual <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_Lights_(Berlin)" title="Festival of Lights (Berlin)">Festival of Lights</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin's nightlife has been celebrated as one of the most diverse and vibrant of its kind.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> In the 1970s and 80s the <a href="/wiki/SO36" title="SO36">SO36</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg" title="Kreuzberg">Kreuzberg</a> was a centre for <a href="/wiki/Punk_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Punk music">punk music</a> and culture. The <i>SOUND</i> and the <i>Dschungel</i> gained notoriety. Throughout the 1990s, people in their 20s from all over the world, particularly those in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, made Berlin's club scene a premier nightlife venue. After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Berlin_Wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Berlin Wall">fall of the Berlin Wall</a> in 1989, many historic buildings in Mitte, the former city centre of East Berlin, were illegally occupied and re-built by young squatters and became a fertile ground for underground and <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">counterculture</a> gatherings. The central boroughs are home to many nightclubs, including the Watergate, <a href="/wiki/Tresor" title="Tresor">Tresor</a>, <a href="/wiki/E-Werk" title="E-Werk">E-Werk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berghain" title="Berghain">Berghain</a>. The <a href="/wiki/KitKatClub" title="KitKatClub">KitKatClub</a> and several other locations are known for their sexually uninhibited parties.</p>
<p>Clubs are not required to close at a fixed time during the weekends, and many parties last well into the morning, or even all weekend. The <i>Berghain</i> features the well-known <i>Panorama Bar</i>, a bar that opens its shades at daybreak, allowing party-goers a panorama view of Berlin after dancing through the night. The <i>Weekend Club</i> near <a href="/wiki/Alexanderplatz" title="Alexanderplatz">Alexanderplatz</a> features a roof terrace that allows partying at night. Several venues have become a popular stage for the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Burlesque" title="Neo-Burlesque">Neo-Burlesque</a> scene.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:In_Berghain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/In_Berghain.jpg/220px-In_Berghain.jpg" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/In_Berghain.jpg/330px-In_Berghain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/In_Berghain.jpg/440px-In_Berghain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="351" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:In_Berghain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Berghain" title="Berghain">Berghain</a> nightclub</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has a long history of gay culture, and is an important <a href="/wiki/Scientific-Humanitarian_Committee" title="Scientific-Humanitarian Committee">birthplace of the LGBT rights movement</a>. Same-sex bars and dance halls operated freely as early as the 1880s, and the first gay magazine, <i>Der Eigene</i>, started in 1896. By the 1920s, gays and lesbians had an unprecedented visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-Krauss_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krauss-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_New_Yorker_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_New_Yorker-169">[169]</a></sup> Today, in addition to a positive atmosphere in the wider club scene, the city again has a huge number of queer clubs and festivals. The most famous and largest are <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Pride" title="Berlin Pride">Berlin Pride</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Street_Day" title="Christopher Street Day">Christopher Street Day</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Lesbian_and_Gay_City_Festival" title="Lesbian and Gay City Festival">Lesbian and Gay City Festival</a> in Berlin-Schöneberg, the <a href="/wiki/Kreuzberg_Pride" title="Kreuzberg Pride">Kreuzberg Pride</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hustlaball" class="mw-redirect" title="Hustlaball">Hustlaball</a>.</p>
<p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="Berlin International Film Festival">Berlin International Film Festival</a> (Berlinale) with around 500,000 admissions is considered to be the largest publicly attended film festival in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The Karneval der Kulturen (<i>Carnival of Cultures</i>), a multi-ethnic street parade, is celebrated every <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a> weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Berlin is also well known for the cultural festival, <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Festspiele" title="Berliner Festspiele">Berliner Festspiele</a>, which includes the jazz festival <a href="/wiki/JazzFest_Berlin" title="JazzFest Berlin">JazzFest Berlin</a>. Several technology and media art festivals and conferences are held in the city, including <a href="/wiki/Transmediale" title="Transmediale">Transmediale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chaos_Communication_Congress" title="Chaos Communication Congress">Chaos Communication Congress</a>. The annual <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Festival" title="Berlin Festival">Berlin Festival</a> focuses on indie rock, electronic music and synthpop and is part of the International Berlin Music Week.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Every year Berlin hosts one of the largest New Year's Eve celebrations in the world, attended by well over a million people. The focal point is the Brandenburg Gate, where midnight fireworks are centred, but various private fireworks displays take place throughout the entire city. Partygoers in Germany often toast the New Year with a glass of <a href="/wiki/Sekt" class="mw-redirect" title="Sekt">sparkling wine</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_in_Berlin" title="Music in Berlin">Music in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg/220px-Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg/330px-Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg/440px-Rattle_BPH-Rittershaus1-Wikipedia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="425" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Sir" title="Sir">Sir</a> <a href="/wiki/Simon_Rattle" title="Simon Rattle">Simon Rattle</a> conducting the renowned <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Philharmonic" title="Berlin Philharmonic">Berlin Philharmonic</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin is home to 44 theaters and stages.<sup id="cite_ref-factsheet_117-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsheet-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Theater_(Berlin)" title="Deutsches Theater (Berlin)">Deutsches Theater</a> in Mitte was built in 1849–50 and has operated almost continuously since then. The <a href="/wiki/Volksb%C3%BChne" title="Volksbühne">Volksbühne</a> at <a href="/wiki/Rosa-Luxemburg-Platz" title="Rosa-Luxemburg-Platz">Rosa-Luxemburg-Platz</a> was built in 1913–14, though the company had been founded in 1890. The <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Ensemble" title="Berliner Ensemble">Berliner Ensemble</a>, famous for performing the works of <a href="/wiki/Bertolt_Brecht" title="Bertolt Brecht">Bertolt Brecht</a>, was established in 1949. The <a href="/wiki/Schaub%C3%BChne" title="Schaubühne">Schaubühne</a> was founded in 1962 and moved to the building of the former Universum Cinema on Kurfürstendamm in 1981. With a seating capacity of 1,895 and a stage floor of 2,854 square metres (30,720 square feet), the <a href="/wiki/Friedrichstadt-Palast" title="Friedrichstadt-Palast">Friedrichstadt-Palast</a> in Berlin Mitte is the largest show palace in Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg/220px-2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg/330px-2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg/440px-2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010-03-13-friedrichstadtpalast-by-RalfR-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dance show at <a href="/wiki/Friedrichstadt-Palast" title="Friedrichstadt-Palast">Friedrichstadt-Palast</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has three major <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera houses</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Oper" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Oper">Deutsche Oper</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_State_Opera" title="Berlin State Opera">Berlin State Opera</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Komische_Oper" class="mw-redirect" title="Komische Oper">Komische Oper</a>. The Berlin State Opera on <a href="/wiki/Unter_den_Linden" title="Unter den Linden">Unter den Linden</a> opened in 1742 and is the oldest of the three. Its current musical director is <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Barenboim" title="Daniel Barenboim">Daniel Barenboim</a>. The Komische Oper has traditionally specialized in <a href="/wiki/Operetta" title="Operetta">operettas</a> and is located at Unter den Linden as well. The Deutsche Oper opened in 1912 in Charlottenburg.</p>
<p>The city's main venue for musical theater performances are the Theater am Potsdamer Platz and <a href="/wiki/Theater_des_Westens" title="Theater des Westens">Theater des Westens</a> (built in 1895). Contemporary dance can be seen at the <i>Radialsystem V</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Tempodrom" title="Tempodrom">Tempodrom</a> is host to concerts and circus inspired entertainment. It also houses a multi-sensory spa experience. The <a href="/wiki/Admiralspalast" title="Admiralspalast">Admiralspalast</a> in Mitte has a vibrant program of <a href="/wiki/Variety_show" title="Variety show">variety</a> and music events.</p>
<p>There are seven symphony orchestras in Berlin. The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Philharmonic_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Philharmonic Orchestra">Berlin Philharmonic Orchestra</a> is one of the preeminent orchestras in the world;<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> it is housed in the <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Philharmonie" title="Berliner Philharmonie">Berliner Philharmonie</a> near Potsdamer Platz on a street named for the orchestra's longest-serving conductor, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_von_Karajan" title="Herbert von Karajan">Herbert von Karajan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The current principal conductor is <a href="/wiki/Simon_Rattle" title="Simon Rattle">Simon Rattle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Konzerthausorchester_Berlin" title="Konzerthausorchester Berlin">Konzerthausorchester Berlin</a> was founded in 1952 as the orchestra for East Berlin. Its current principal conductor is <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Fischer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan Fischer">Ivan Fischer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Haus_der_Kulturen_der_Welt" title="Haus der Kulturen der Welt">Haus der Kulturen der Welt</a> presents various exhibitions dealing with intercultural issues and stages world music and conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> The <i>Kookaburra</i> and the <i>Quatsch Comedy Club</i> are known for satire and <a href="/wiki/Stand-up_comedy" title="Stand-up comedy">stand-up comedy</a> shows.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">German cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg/220px-Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg/330px-Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg/440px-Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin-Mitte_Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Currywurst_Museum" title="Deutsches Currywurst Museum">Currywurst Museum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">cuisine</a> and culinary offerings of Berlin vary greatly. Twelve restaurants in Berlin have been included in the <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin Guide</a> of 2015, which ranks the city at the top for the number of restaurants having this distinction in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Berlin is well known for its offerings of <a href="/wiki/Vegetarianism" title="Vegetarianism">vegetarian</a><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">vegan</a> <sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> cuisine and is home to an innovative entrepreneurial food scene promoting cosmopolitan flavors, local and sustainable ingredients, pop-up street food markets, supper clubs, as well as food festivals, such as Berlin Food Week.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many local foods originated from north German culinary traditions and include rustic and hearty dishes with pork, goose, fish, peas, beans, cucumbers, or potatoes. Typical Berliner fare include popular <a href="/wiki/Street_food" title="Street food">street food</a> like the <i><a href="/wiki/Currywurst" title="Currywurst">Currywurst</a></i> (which gained popularity with post-war construction workers rebuilding the city), <i><a href="/wiki/Frikadeller" title="Frikadeller">Buletten</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Berliner_(doughnut)" title="Berliner (doughnut)">Berliner</a></i> doughnut, known in Berlin as <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Pfannkuchen</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> German bakeries offering a variety of breads and pastries are widespread. One of Europe's largest <a href="/wiki/Delicatessen" title="Delicatessen">delicatessen</a> markets is found at the <a href="/wiki/KaDeWe" class="mw-redirect" title="KaDeWe">KaDeWe</a>, and among the world’s largest chocolate stores is <i>Fassbender &amp; Rausch</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Berlin is also home to a diverse gastronomy scene reflecting the immigrant history of the city. Turkish and Arab immigrants brought their culinary traditions to the city, such as the <a href="/wiki/Lahmajoun" title="Lahmajoun">lahmajoun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falafel" title="Falafel">falafel</a>, which have become common fast food staples. The modern fast food version of the <a href="/wiki/Doner_kebab" title="Doner kebab">doner kebab</a> sandwich <a href="/wiki/Kadir_Nurman" title="Kadir Nurman">evolved in Berlin</a> in the 1970s, and became a favorite in Germany and elsewhere in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-188">[188]</a></sup> Asian cuisine like Chinese, Vietnamese, Thai, Indian, Korean, and Japanese restaurants, as well as Spanish tapas bars, Italian, and Greek cuisine, can be found in many parts of the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoo041.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Zoo041.jpg/220px-Zoo041.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Zoo041.jpg/330px-Zoo041.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Zoo041.jpg/440px-Zoo041.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoo041.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elephant Gate at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Zoological_Garden" title="Berlin Zoological Garden">Berlin Zoo</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Berlin_Zoological_Garden" title="Berlin Zoological Garden">Zoologischer Garten Berlin</a>, the older of two zoos in the city, was founded in 1844. It is the most visited zoo in Europe and presents the most diverse range of species in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> It was the home of the captive-born celebrity polar bear <a href="/wiki/Knut_(polar_bear)" title="Knut (polar bear)">Knut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-knutbbc1_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knutbbc1-190">[190]</a></sup> The city's other zoo, <a href="/wiki/Tierpark_Berlin" title="Tierpark Berlin">Tierpark Friedrichsfelde</a>, was founded in 1955.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Berlin-Dahlem_Botanical_Garden_and_Botanical_Museum" title="Berlin-Dahlem Botanical Garden and Botanical Museum">Berlin's Botanischer Garten</a> includes the Botanic Museum Berlin. With an area of 43 hectares (110 acres) and around 22,000 different plant species, it is one of the largest and most diverse collections of botanical life in the world. Other gardens in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Britzer_Garten" title="Britzer Garten">Britzer Garten</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Erholungspark_Marzahn" title="Erholungspark Marzahn">Gärten der Welt</a> (Gardens of the World) in Marzahn.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten,_Berlin" title="Tiergarten, Berlin">Tiergarten</a>, located in Mitte, is Berlin's largest park and was designed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Joseph_Lenn%C3%A9" title="Peter Joseph Lenné">Peter Joseph Lenné</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In Kreuzberg, the <a href="/wiki/Viktoriapark" title="Viktoriapark">Viktoriapark</a> provides a viewing point over the southern part of inner-city Berlin. <a href="/wiki/Treptower_Park" title="Treptower Park">Treptower Park</a>, beside the Spree in <a href="/wiki/Treptow" title="Treptow">Treptow</a>, features a large <a href="/wiki/Soviet_War_Memorial_(Treptower_Park)" title="Soviet War Memorial (Treptower Park)">Soviet War Memorial</a>. The Volkspark in <a href="/wiki/Friedrichshain" title="Friedrichshain">Friedrichshain</a>, which opened in 1848, is the oldest park in the city, with monuments, a summer outdoor cinema and several sports areas.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Potsdam" title="Potsdam">Potsdam</a> is situated on the southwestern periphery of Berlin. The city was a residence of the <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a> kings and the <a href="/wiki/German_Emperor" title="German Emperor">German Kaiser</a>, until 1918. The area around Potsdam in particular <a href="/wiki/Sanssouci" title="Sanssouci">Sanssouci</a> is known for a series of interconnected lakes and cultural landmarks. The <a href="/wiki/Palaces_and_Parks_of_Potsdam_and_Berlin" title="Palaces and Parks of Potsdam and Berlin">Palaces and Parks of Potsdam and Berlin</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>Berlin is also well known for its numerous cafés, street musicians, beach bars along the Spree River, flea markets, boutique shops and <a href="/wiki/Pop_up_store" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop up store">pop up stores</a>, which are a source for recreation and leisure.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Berlin" title="Sport in Berlin">Sport in Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Berlin" title="Football in Berlin">Football in Berlin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg/220px-Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg/330px-Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg/440px-Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7149" data-file-height="3920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berliner_Olympiastadion_night_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Berlin)" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Stadium (Berlin)">Olympiastadion</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Final">2006 FIFA World Cup Final</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_marathon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Berlin_marathon.jpg/220px-Berlin_marathon.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Berlin_marathon.jpg/330px-Berlin_marathon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Berlin_marathon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="419" data-file-height="303" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_marathon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Marathon" title="Berlin Marathon">Berlin Marathon</a> is the current world record course.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Berlin has established a high-profile as a host city of major international sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The city hosted the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> and was the host city for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> final.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IAAF_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="IAAF World Championships in Athletics">IAAF World Championships in Athletics</a> was held in the <a href="/wiki/Olympiastadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympiastadion">Olympiastadion</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The city hosted the Basketball <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Final_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroleague Final Four">Euroleague Final Four</a> in <a href="/wiki/2009_Euroleague_Final_Four" title="2009 Euroleague Final Four">2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Euroleague_Final_Four" title="2016 Euroleague Final Four">2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> and was one of the hosts of the FIBA <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2015" title="EuroBasket 2015">EuroBasket 2015</a>. In 2015 Berlin became the venue for the <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2015 UEFA Champions League Final">UEFA Champions League Final</a>.</p>
<p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Marathon" title="Berlin Marathon">Berlin Marathon</a>&#160;–  a course that holds the most top-10 world record runs&#160;–  and the <a href="/wiki/Internationales_Stadionfest" class="mw-redirect" title="Internationales Stadionfest">ISTAF</a> are well-established athletic events in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mellowpark" title="Mellowpark">Mellowpark</a> in Köpenick is one of the biggest skate and BMX parks in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> A Fan Fest at Brandenburg Gate, which attracts several hundred-thousand spectators, has become popular during international football competitions, like the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013 around 600,000 Berliners were registered in one of the more than 2,300 sport and fitness clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The city of Berlin operates more than 60 public indoor and outdoor swimming pools.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Berlin is the largest Olympic training centre in Germany. About 500 top athletes (15% of all German top athletes) are based there. Forty-seven elite athletes participated in the 2012 Summer Olympics. Berliners would achieve seven gold, twelve silver and three bronze medals.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several professional clubs representing the most important spectator team sports in Germany have their base in Berlin:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Population11-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Population11_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.statistik-berlin-brandenburg.de/pms/2017/17-02-24a.pdf">"Amt für Statistik Berlin Brandenburg"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i><a href="/wiki/Amt_f%C3%BCr_Statistik_Berlin-Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Amt für Statistik Berlin-Brandenburg">Amt für Statistik Berlin-Brandenburg</a></i> (in German). 2016<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">28 February</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABerlin&amp;rft.atitle=Amt+f%C3%BCr+Statistik+Berlin+Brandenburg&amp;rft.date=2016&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Amt+f%C3%BCr+Statistik+Berlin-Brandenburg&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.statistik-berlin-brandenburg.de%2Fpms%2F2017%2F17-02-24a.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Prefixes for vehicle registration were introduced in 1906, but often changed due to the political changes after 1945. Vehicles were registered under the following prefixes: "I A" (1906&#160;– April 1945; devalidated on 11 August 1945); no prefix, only digits (from July to August 1945), "БГ" (=BG; 1945–46, for cars, lorries and busses), "ГФ" (=GF; 1945–46, for cars, lorries and busses), "БM" (=BM; 1945–47, for motor bikes), "ГM" (=GM; 1945–47, for motor bikes), "KB" (i.e.: <a href="/wiki/Allied_Kommandatura" title="Allied Kommandatura">Kommandatura</a> of Berlin; for all of Berlin 1947–48, continued for <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> until 1956), "GB" (i.e.: Greater Berlin, for <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a> 1948–53), "I" (for East Berlin, 1953–90), "B" (for West Berlin from 1 July 1956, continued for all of Berlin since 1990).</span></li>

<tr>
<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">1,000,000+</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Berlin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a></li>

<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd plainlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px;text-align:left;">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 14em; -webkit-column-width: 14em; column-width: 14em;">
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics" title="1896 Summer Olympics">1896</a>:</b> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece"><img alt="Greece" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Greece_%281822-1978%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/1900_Summer_Olympics" title="1900 Summer Olympics">1900</a>:</b> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a></li>

<div id="Host_cities_of_the_IAAF_World_Championships_in_Athletics" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">Host cities of the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="IAAF World Championships in Athletics">IAAF World Championships in Athletics</a></div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1983_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1983 World Championships in Athletics">1983</a>: <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1987_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1987 World Championships in Athletics">1987</a>: <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1991_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1991 World Championships in Athletics">1991</a>: <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1993_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1993 World Championships in Athletics">1993</a>: <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics">1995</a>: <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1997_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1997 World Championships in Athletics">1997</a>: <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1999_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1999 World Championships in Athletics">1999</a>: <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2001_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2001 World Championships in Athletics">2001</a>: <a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2003_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2003 World Championships in Athletics">2003</a>: <a href="/wiki/Saint-Denis,_Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Saint-Denis, Seine-Saint-Denis">Saint-Denis</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2005_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2005 World Championships in Athletics">2005</a>: <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2007_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2007 World Championships in Athletics">2007</a>: <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2009_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2009 World Championships in Athletics">2009</a>: <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Berlin</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2011_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2011 World Championships in Athletics">2011</a>: <a href="/wiki/Daegu" title="Daegu">Daegu</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2013_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2013 World Championships in Athletics">2013</a>: <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015</a>: <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2017_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2017 World Championships in Athletics">2017</a>: <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2019_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2019 World Championships in Athletics">2019</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a></i></span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2021_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2021 World Championships in Athletics">2021</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene</a></i></span></li>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.4em;line-height:1.25em;">
<div>
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
</ul>
